      <p><b>North Macedonia</b><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[c]</a></sup> (<b>Macedonia</b> until February 2019), officially the <b>Republic of North Macedonia</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[d]</a></sup> is a country in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeast Europe</a>. It gained independence in 1991 as one of the successor states of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>. North Macedonia is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> bordering with <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a><sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo-13">[e]</a></sup> to the northwest, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> to the south, and <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> to the west.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[9]</a></sup> It constitutes approximately the northern third of the larger geographical <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(region)" title="Macedonia (region)">region of Macedonia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Skopje" title="Skopje">Skopje</a>, the capital and largest city, is home to a quarter of the country's 2.06&nbsp;million population. The majority of the residents are ethnic <a href="/wiki/Macedonians_(ethnic_group)" title="Macedonians (ethnic group)">Macedonians</a>, a <a href="/wiki/South_Slavs" title="South Slavs">South Slavic people</a>. <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_North_Macedonia" title="Albanians in North Macedonia">Albanians</a> form a significant minority at around 25%, followed by <a href="/wiki/Turks_in_North_Macedonia" title="Turks in North Macedonia">Turks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_North_Macedonia" title="Romani people in North Macedonia">Romani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbs_in_North_Macedonia" title="Serbs in North Macedonia">Serbs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks_in_North_Macedonia" title="Bosniaks in North Macedonia">Bosniaks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aromanians_in_North_Macedonia" title="Aromanians in North Macedonia">Aromanians</a> (the latter including <a href="/wiki/Megleno-Romanians" title="Megleno-Romanians">Megleno-Romanians</a> in official statistics). </p>
      <p>The history of the region begins with the <a href="/wiki/Paeonia_(kingdom)" title="Paeonia (kingdom)">kingdom of Paeonia</a>, a mixed <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thraco</a>-<a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyrian</a> polity.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[10]</a></sup> In the late sixth century BC, the area was subjugated by the Persian <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a>, then incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(ancient_kingdom)" title="Macedonia (ancient kingdom)">kingdom of Macedonia</a> in the fourth century BC. <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">The Romans</a> conquered the region in the second century BC and made it part of the larger province of <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(Roman_province)" title="Macedonia (Roman province)">Macedonia</a>. The area remained part of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>, but was often raided and settled by <a href="/wiki/Early_Slavs" title="Early Slavs">Slavic tribes</a> beginning in the sixth century of the Christian era. Following <a href="/wiki/Byzantine%E2%80%93Bulgarian_wars" title="ByzantineâBulgarian wars">centuries of contention</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Empire" title="Bulgarian Empire">Bulgarian</a>, Byzantine, and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Empire" title="Serbian Empire">Serbian Empire</a>, it was part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> dominion from the mid-14th until the early 20th century, when, following the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a> of 1912 and 1913, the modern territory of North Macedonia came under <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Serbian</a> rule. </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>, it was ruled by Bulgaria, but after the end of the war it returned to being under Serbian rule as part of the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbs,_Croats_and_Slovenes" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenes">Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenes</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_in_Yugoslav_Macedonia" title="World War II in Yugoslav Macedonia">Second World War</a>, it was ruled by Bulgaria again and in 1945 it was established as a <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Socialist Republic of Macedonia">constituent state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">communist Yugoslavia</a>, which it remained until <a href="/wiki/1991_Macedonian_independence_referendum" title="1991 Macedonian independence referendum">its peaceful secession in 1991</a>. The country became a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in April 1993, but as a result of a <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_naming_dispute" title="Macedonia naming dispute">dispute with Greece</a> over the name "Macedonia", it was admitted under the provisional description "the former Yugoslav Republic of Macedonia"<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[f]</a></sup> (abbreviated as "FYR Macedonia" or "FYROM"). In June 2018, Macedonia and Greece resolved the dispute with <a href="/wiki/Prespa_agreement" title="Prespa agreement">an agreement</a> that the country should rename itself "Republic of North Macedonia". This renaming came into effect in February 2019. </p>
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitutional</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>, North Macedonia is a member of the UN, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_European_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Central European Free Trade Agreement">CEFTA</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a>. Since 2005, it has also been a <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_North_Macedonia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of North Macedonia to the European Union">candidate for joining the European Union</a>. North Macedonia is an upper-middle-income country<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[13]</a></sup> and has undergone considerable economic reform since independence in developing an <a href="/wiki/Open_economy" title="Open economy">open economy</a>. North Macedonia is a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a>, ranking 82nd on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, and provides a <a href="/wiki/Social_security" class="mw-redirect" title="Social security">social security</a>, <a href="/wiki/Health_in_North_Macedonia" title="Health in North Macedonia">universal health care</a> system, and free <a href="/wiki/Education_in_North_Macedonia" title="Education in North Macedonia">primary and secondary education</a> to its citizens. </p>

         </ul> </li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names_and_etymology"><span class="anchor" id="Names"></span><span class="anchor" id="Etymology"></span><span class="anchor" id="Names_and_etymology"></span>Names and etymology</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(terminology)" title="Macedonia (terminology)">Macedonia (terminology)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_naming_dispute" title="Macedonia naming dispute">Macedonia naming dispute</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The state's name derives from the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> word <span lang="el" title="Greek-language text"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%9C%CE%B1%CE%BA%CE%B5%CE%B4%CE%BF%CE%BD%CE%AF%CE%B1#Greek" class="extiw" title="wikt:ÎÎ±ÎºÎµÎ´Î¿Î½Î¯Î±">ÎÎ±ÎºÎµÎ´Î¿Î½Î¯Î±</a></span> (<i>MakedonÃ­a</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Macedonia_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macedonia-21">[15]</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Macedon" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedon">kingdom</a> (later, <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(region)" title="Macedonia (region)">region</a>) named after the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Macedonians" title="Ancient Macedonians">ancient Macedonians</a>. Their name, <span lang="el" title="Greek-language text"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%9C%CE%B1%CE%BA%CE%B5%CE%B4%CF%8C%CE%BD%CE%B5%CF%82#Greek" class="extiw" title="wikt:ÎÎ±ÎºÎµÎ´ÏÎ½ÎµÏ">ÎÎ±ÎºÎµÎ´ÏÎ½ÎµÏ</a></span> (<i>MakedÃ³nes</i>), ultimately derives from the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">ancient Greek</a> adjective <a href="/wiki/Makednos" class="mw-redirect" title="Makednos">Î¼Î±ÎºÎµÎ´Î½ÏÏ</a> (<i>makednÃ³s</i>), meaning 'tall' or 'taper',<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[16]</a></sup> which shares the same root as the adjective <span lang="el" title="Greek-language text"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%BC%CE%B1%CE%BA%CF%81%CF%8C%CF%82#Greek" class="extiw" title="wikt:Î¼Î±ÎºÏÏÏ">Î¼Î±ÎºÏÏÏ</a></span> (<i>makrÃ³s</i>, 'long, tall, high') in ancient Greek.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[17]</a></sup> The name is believed to have originally meant either 'highlanders' or 'the tall ones', possibly descriptive of the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Macedonians" title="Ancient Macedonians">people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Macedonia_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macedonia-21">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[19]</a></sup> According to linguist <a href="/wiki/Robert_S._P._Beekes" title="Robert S. P. Beekes">Robert S. P. Beekes</a>, both terms are of <a href="/wiki/Pre-Greek_substrate" title="Pre-Greek substrate">Pre-Greek substrate</a> origin and cannot be explained in terms of Indo-European morphology;<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[20]</a></sup> however, according to linguist Filip De Decker, Beekes's arguments are insufficient.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the early 19th century, the name of Macedonia was almost unknown in the modern-day area.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[24]</a></sup> It was revived only in middle of the century, with the <a href="/wiki/Rise_of_nationalism_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Rise of nationalism in the Ottoman Empire">rise of nationalism in the Ottoman Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[27]</a></sup> In the early 20th century the region was already a national cause, contested among Bulgarian, Greek and Serbian nationalists. During the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">interwar period</a> the use of the name <i>Macedonia</i> was prohibited in the Kingdom of Yugoslavia, due to the implemented policy of <a href="/wiki/Serbianisation" title="Serbianisation">Serbianisation</a> of the local Slavic-speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[29]</a></sup> The name <i>Macedonia</i> was adopted officially for the first time at the end of the Second World War by the new <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Socialist Republic of Macedonia">Socialist Republic of Macedonia</a>, which became one of the six constituent countries of the Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia. After the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Communism" class="mw-redirect" title="Fall of Communism">fall of Communism</a>, with the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia" title="Breakup of Yugoslavia">breakup of Yugoslavia</a>, this federal entity declared independence and changed its official name to Republic of Macedonia in 1991. Prior to June 2018, the use of the name <i>Macedonia</i> was <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_naming_dispute" title="Macedonia naming dispute">disputed between Greece and the then-Republic of Macedonia</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Prespa_agreement" title="Prespa agreement">Prespa agreement</a> of June 2018 saw the country change its name to the <i>Republic of North Macedonia</i> eight months later.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[31]</a></sup> A non-binding<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2018_Macedonian_referendum" title="2018 Macedonian referendum">national referendum</a> on the matter passed with 90% approval but did not reach the required 50% turnout amidst a boycott, leaving the final decision with parliament to ratify the result.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[33]</a></sup> Parliament approved of the name change on 19 October, reaching the required two-thirds majority needed to enact constitutional changes.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[34]</a></sup> The vote to amend the constitution and change the name of the country passed on 11 January 2019 in favour of the amendment.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[35]</a></sup> The amendment entered into force on 12 February, following the ratification of the Prespa agreement and the Protocol on the Accession of North Macedonia to NATO by the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Parliament">Greek Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[36]</a></sup> Despite the renaming, the country is unofficially referred to as 'Macedonia' by its citizens and most of the local media outlets.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_North_Macedonia" title="History of North Macedonia">History of North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Historiography_in_North_Macedonia" title="Historiography in North Macedonia">Historiography in North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Paeonia_(kingdom)" title="Paeonia (kingdom)">Paeonia (kingdom)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(ancient_kingdom)" title="Macedonia (ancient kingdom)">Macedonia (ancient kingdom)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Dardania" title="Kingdom of Dardania">Kingdom of Dardania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Paeon_founder_of_Paeonia_Son_of_Endymion_Greek_Mythology_Map_(English).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Paeon_founder_of_Paeonia_Son_of_Endymion_Greek_Mythology_Map_%28English%29.svg/220px-Paeon_founder_of_Paeonia_Son_of_Endymion_Greek_Mythology_Map_%28English%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Paeon_founder_of_Paeonia_Son_of_Endymion_Greek_Mythology_Map_%28English%29.svg/330px-Paeon_founder_of_Paeonia_Son_of_Endymion_Greek_Mythology_Map_%28English%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Paeon_founder_of_Paeonia_Son_of_Endymion_Greek_Mythology_Map_%28English%29.svg/440px-Paeon_founder_of_Paeonia_Son_of_Endymion_Greek_Mythology_Map_%28English%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="994" data-file-height="793"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Paeon_founder_of_Paeonia_Son_of_Endymion_Greek_Mythology_Map_(English).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Paeonian_tribes" class="mw-redirect" title="Paeonian tribes">Paeonian tribes</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>North Macedonia geographically roughly corresponds to the ancient <a href="/wiki/Paeonia_(kingdom)" title="Paeonia (kingdom)">kingdom of Paeonia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[40]</a></sup> which was located immediately north of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(ancient_kingdom)" title="Macedonia (ancient kingdom)">kingdom of Macedonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[41]</a></sup> Paeonia was inhabited by the Paeonians, a <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracian</a> <a href="/wiki/People" title="People">people</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[42]</a></sup> whilst the northwest was inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Dardani" title="Dardani">Dardani</a> and the southwest by tribes known historically as the <a href="/wiki/Enchelei" class="mw-redirect" title="Enchelei">Enchelae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pelagones" class="mw-redirect" title="Pelagones">Pelagones</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lynkestis" title="Lynkestis">Lyncestae</a>; the latter two are generally regarded as <a href="/wiki/Molossians" title="Molossians">Molossian</a> tribes of the northwestern <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a> group, whilst the former two are considered <a href="/wiki/Illyrian_tribes" class="mw-redirect" title="Illyrian tribes">Illyrian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the late 6th century BC, the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Achaemenid Persia">Achaemenid Persians</a> under <a href="/wiki/Darius_the_Great" title="Darius the Great">Darius the Great</a> conquered the <a href="/wiki/Paeonia_(kingdom)" title="Paeonia (kingdom)">Paeonians</a>, incorporating what is today North Macedonia within their vast territories.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoweReames2008239_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoweReames2008239-55">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoismanWorthington2011135â138,_342â345_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoismanWorthington2011135â138,_342â345-56">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[51]</a></sup> Following the loss in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Persian_invasion_of_Greece" title="Second Persian invasion of Greece">Second Persian invasion of Greece</a> in 479 BC, the Persians eventually withdrew from their European territories, including from what is today North Macedonia. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ancientbitola.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Ancientbitola.jpg/220px-Ancientbitola.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Ancientbitola.jpg/330px-Ancientbitola.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Ancientbitola.jpg/440px-Ancientbitola.jpg 2x" data-file-width="556" data-file-height="369"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ancientbitola.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Heraclea_Lyncestis" title="Heraclea Lyncestis">Heraclea Lyncestis</a>, a city founded by <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Macedon" title="Philip II of Macedon">Philip II of Macedon</a> in the 4th century BC; ruins of the Byzantine "Small Basilica"
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Macedon" title="Philip II of Macedon">Philip II of Macedon</a> absorbed<sup id="cite_ref-Rome_page_75_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rome_page_75-58">[52]</a></sup> the regions of <a href="/wiki/Upper_Macedonia" title="Upper Macedonia">Upper Macedonia</a> (Lynkestis and Pelagonia) and the southern part of Paeonia (<a href="/wiki/Deuriopus" title="Deuriopus">Deuriopus</a>) into the kingdom of Macedon in 356 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[53]</a></sup> Philip's son <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> conquered the remainder of the region and incorporated it in his empire, reaching as far north as <a href="/wiki/Scupi" title="Scupi">Scupi</a>, but the city and the surrounding area remained part of <a href="/wiki/Dardania_(Roman_province)" title="Dardania (Roman province)">Dardania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">The Romans</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(Roman_province)" title="Macedonia (Roman province)">province of Macedonia</a> in 146 BC. By the time of <a href="/wiki/Diocletian" title="Diocletian">Diocletian</a>, the province had been subdivided between <i>Macedonia Prima</i> ("first Macedonia") on the south, encompassing most of the kingdom of Macedon, and <i>Macedonia Salutaris</i> (meaning "wholesome Macedonia", known also as <i>Macedonia Secunda</i>, "second Macedonia") on the north, encompassing partially Dardania and the whole of Paeonia; most of the country's modern boundaries fell within the latter, with the city of <a href="/wiki/Stobi" title="Stobi">Stobi</a> as its capital.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[55]</a></sup> Roman expansion brought the Scupi area under Roman rule in the time of <a href="/wiki/Domitian" title="Domitian">Domitian</a> (81â96 AD), and it fell within the Province of <a href="/wiki/Moesia" title="Moesia">Moesia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[56]</a></sup> Whilst <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> remained the dominant language in the eastern part of the Roman empire, especially south of <a href="/wiki/Jire%C4%8Dek_Line" title="JireÄek Line">JireÄek Line</a>, Latin spread to some extent in Macedonia.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_period">Medieval period</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sclaveni" title="Sclaveni">Sclaveni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_(theme)" title="Bulgaria (theme)">Bulgaria (theme)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Empire" title="Serbian Empire">Serbian Empire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Vardar_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Vardar Macedonia">Ottoman Vardar Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:66-manasses-chronicle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/66-manasses-chronicle.jpg/170px-66-manasses-chronicle.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/66-manasses-chronicle.jpg/255px-66-manasses-chronicle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/66-manasses-chronicle.jpg/340px-66-manasses-chronicle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2351" data-file-height="3259"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:66-manasses-chronicle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Miniature from the <a href="/wiki/Constantine_Manasses" title="Constantine Manasses">Manasses Chronicle</a>, depicting the defeat of <a href="/wiki/Samuel_of_Bulgaria" title="Samuel of Bulgaria">Samuil</a> by <a href="/wiki/Basil_II" title="Basil II">Basil II</a> and the return of his blinded soldiers
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Early_Slavs" title="Early Slavs">Slavic tribes</a> settled in the Balkan region including North Macedonia by the late 6th century AD. During the 580s, Byzantine literature attests to the Slavs raiding Byzantine territories in the region of Macedonia, later aided by <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a>. Historical records document that in <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">â680</span> a group of Bulgars, Slavs and Byzantines led by a Bulgar called <a href="/wiki/Kuber" title="Kuber">Kuber</a> settled in the region of the Keramisian plain, centred on the city of <a href="/wiki/Bitola" title="Bitola">Bitola</a>, forming a second route for the Bulgar definitive settlement on the Balkan Peninsula at the end of the 7th century.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[58]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Presian_I_of_Bulgaria" title="Presian I of Bulgaria">Presian</a>'s reign apparently coincides with the extension of Bulgarian control over the Slavic tribes in and around Macedonia. The Slavic tribes that settled in the region of Macedonia converted to Christianity around the 9th century during the reign of Tsar <a href="/wiki/Boris_I_of_Bulgaria" title="Boris I of Bulgaria">Boris I of Bulgaria</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ohrid_Literary_School" title="Ohrid Literary School">Ohrid Literary School</a> became one of the two major cultural centres of the First Bulgarian Empire, along with the <a href="/wiki/Preslav_Literary_School" title="Preslav Literary School">Preslav Literary School</a>. Established in Ohrid in 886 by Saint <a href="/wiki/Clement_of_Ohrid" title="Clement of Ohrid">Clement of Ohrid</a> on the order of Boris I, the Ohrid Literary School was involved in the spreading of the <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">Cyrillic script</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:St_Sophia_(Ohrid).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Colored dice with white background" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/St_Sophia_%28Ohrid%29.jpg/220px-St_Sophia_%28Ohrid%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/St_Sophia_%28Ohrid%29.jpg/330px-St_Sophia_%28Ohrid%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/St_Sophia_%28Ohrid%29.jpg/440px-St_Sophia_%28Ohrid%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5457" data-file-height="3414"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_San_Pantale%C3%B3n,_Ohrid,_Macedonia,_2014-04-17,_DD_35_HDR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Colored dice with checkered background" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Iglesia_de_San_Pantale%C3%B3n%2C_Ohrid%2C_Macedonia%2C_2014-04-17%2C_DD_35_HDR.jpg/220px-Iglesia_de_San_Pantale%C3%B3n%2C_Ohrid%2C_Macedonia%2C_2014-04-17%2C_DD_35_HDR.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Iglesia_de_San_Pantale%C3%B3n%2C_Ohrid%2C_Macedonia%2C_2014-04-17%2C_DD_35_HDR.jpg/330px-Iglesia_de_San_Pantale%C3%B3n%2C_Ohrid%2C_Macedonia%2C_2014-04-17%2C_DD_35_HDR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Iglesia_de_San_Pantale%C3%B3n%2C_Ohrid%2C_Macedonia%2C_2014-04-17%2C_DD_35_HDR.jpg/440px-Iglesia_de_San_Pantale%C3%B3n%2C_Ohrid%2C_Macedonia%2C_2014-04-17%2C_DD_35_HDR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4713" data-file-height="3258"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._Sophia,_Ohrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Church of St. Sophia, Ohrid">Church of St. Sophia</a>, the first synod church of the <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Ohrid" title="Archbishopric of Ohrid">Archbishopric of Ohrid</a> (top). The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Saints_Clement_and_Panteleimon" title="Church of Saints Clement and Panteleimon">Church of Saints Clement and Panteleimon</a> (bottom). Both churches are located in <a href="/wiki/Ohrid" title="Ohrid">Ohrid</a>.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After <a href="/wiki/Sviatoslav%27s_invasion_of_Bulgaria" title="Sviatoslav's invasion of Bulgaria">Sviatoslav's invasion of Bulgaria</a>, the Byzantines took control of East Bulgaria. <a href="/wiki/Samuel_of_Bulgaria" title="Samuel of Bulgaria">Samuil</a>, one of the Cometopuli brothers, was proclaimed <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">Tsar of Bulgaria</a>. He moved the capital to Skopje and then to Ohrid, which had been the cultural and military centre of southwestern Bulgaria since Boris I's rule. Samuil reestablished Bulgarian power, but after several decades of conflicts, in 1014, the Byzantine Emperor <a href="/wiki/Basil_II" title="Basil II">Basil II</a> defeated his armies, and within four years the Byzantines restored control over the Balkans (including North Macedonia) for the first time since the 7th century. The rank of the autocephalous <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Patriarchate" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian Patriarchate">Bulgarian Patriarchate</a> was lowered due to its subjugation to <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarch_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople">Constantinople</a> and it was transformed into the <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Ohrid" title="Archbishopric of Ohrid">Archbishopric of Ohrid</a>. By the late 12th century, Byzantine decline saw the region contested by various political entities, including a brief <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">Norman</a> occupation in the 1080s. </p>
      <p>In the early 13th century, a revived <a href="/wiki/Second_Bulgarian_Empire" title="Second Bulgarian Empire">Bulgarian Empire</a> gained control of the region. Plagued by political difficulties, the empire did not last, and the region came once again under Byzantine control in the early 14th century. In the 14th century, it became part of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Empire" title="Serbian Empire">Serbian Empire</a>. Skopje became the capital of Tsar <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Du%C5%A1an" title="Stefan DuÅ¡an">Stefan DuÅ¡an</a>'s empire. Following DuÅ¡an's death, a weak successor appeared, and power struggles between nobles divided the Balkans once again. These events coincided with the entry of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turks" title="Ottoman Turks">Ottoman Turks</a> into Europe. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_period">Ottoman period</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Vardar_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Vardar Macedonia">Ottoman Vardar Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prilep" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Prilep">Kingdom of Prilep</a> was one the short-lived states that emerged from the collapse of the Serbian Empire in the 14th century, which was seized by the Ottomans at the end of the same century.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[60]</a></sup> Gradually, all of the central Balkans were conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and remained under its domination for five centuries as part of the province or <a href="/wiki/Eyalet" title="Eyalet">Eyalet</a> of <a href="/wiki/Rumelia_Eyalet" title="Rumelia Eyalet">Rumelia</a>. The name <i><a href="/wiki/Rumelia" title="Rumelia">Rumelia</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i>Rumeli</i>) means "Land of the Romans" in Turkish, referring to the lands conquered by the Ottoman Turks from the Byzantine Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[61]</a></sup> Over the centuries Rumelia Eyalet was reduced in size through administrative reforms, until by the 19th century it consisted of a region of central Albania and western North Macedonia with its capital at Manastir or present-day <a href="/wiki/Bitola" title="Bitola">Bitola</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eb19_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eb19-68">[62]</a></sup> Rumelia Eyalet was abolished in 1867 and that territory of Macedonia subsequently became part of the province of <a href="/wiki/Manastir_Vilayet" title="Manastir Vilayet">Manastir Vilayet</a> until the end of Ottoman rule in 1912. With the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_National_Revival" title="Bulgarian National Revival">Bulgarian National Revival</a> in the 19th century, many of the reformers were from this region, including the <a href="/wiki/Miladinov_brothers" title="Miladinov brothers">Miladinov brothers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Phillips_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Phillips-69">[63]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rayko_Zhinzifov" title="Rayko Zhinzifov">Rajko Å½inzifov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yoakim_Karchovski" title="Yoakim Karchovski">Joakim KrÄovski</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[64]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kiril_Peychinovich" title="Kiril Peychinovich">Kiril PejÄinoviá¸±</a><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[65]</a></sup> and others. The bishoprics of Skopje, <a href="/wiki/Debar" title="Debar">Debar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bitola" title="Bitola">Bitola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohrid" title="Ohrid">Ohrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veles_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Veles (city)">Veles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Strumica" title="Strumica">Strumica</a> voted to join the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Exarchate" title="Bulgarian Exarchate">Bulgarian Exarchate</a> after it was established in 1870.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[66]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_period">Modern period</span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Macedonian_autonomism">Macedonian autonomism</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Millet" title="Bulgarian Millet">Bulgarian Millet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Autonomy_for_Macedonia_and_Adrianople_regions" title="Autonomy for Macedonia and Adrianople regions">Autonomy for Macedonia and Adrianople regions</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_for_the_Macedonians" title="Macedonia for the Macedonians">Macedonia for the Macedonians</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nikola_Karev.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Nikola_Karev.jpg/170px-Nikola_Karev.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Nikola_Karev.jpg/255px-Nikola_Karev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Nikola_Karev.jpg/340px-Nikola_Karev.jpg 2x" data-file-width="344" data-file-height="469"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nikola_Karev.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Nikola_Karev" title="Nikola Karev">Nikola Karev</a>, head of the provisional government of the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Kru%C5%A1evo_Republic" title="KruÅ¡evo Republic">KruÅ¡evo Republic</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Ilinden_uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="Ilinden uprising">Ilinden uprising</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Several movements whose goals were the establishment of an autonomous Macedonia, which would encompass the entire region of Macedonia, began to arise in the late 19th century; the earliest of these was the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Macedonian-Adrianople_Revolutionary_Committees" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian Macedonian-Adrianople Revolutionary Committees">Bulgarian Macedonian-Adrianople Revolutionary Committees</a>, later becoming Secret Macedonian-Adrianople Revolutionary Organization (SMARO). In 1905 it was renamed the Internal Macedonian-Adrianople Revolutionary Organization (IMARO), and after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> the organisation separated into the <a href="/wiki/Internal_Macedonian_Revolutionary_Organization" title="Internal Macedonian Revolutionary Organization">Internal Macedonian Revolutionary Organization</a> (IMRO) and the <a href="/wiki/Internal_Thracian_Revolutionary_Organisation" title="Internal Thracian Revolutionary Organisation">Internal Thracian Revolutionary Organisation</a> (ITRO).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the early years of the organisation, membership eligibility was exclusive to Bulgarians, but later it was extended to all inhabitants of European Turkey regardless of ethnicity or religion.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[68]</a></sup> The majority of its members were <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Bulgarians" title="Macedonian Bulgarians">Macedonian Bulgarians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[69]</a></sup> In 1903, IMRO organised the <a href="/wiki/Ilinden%E2%80%93Preobrazhenie_Uprising" title="IlindenâPreobrazhenie Uprising">IlindenâPreobrazhenie Uprising</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottomans</a>, which after some initial successes, including the forming of the <a href="/wiki/Kru%C5%A1evo_Republic" title="KruÅ¡evo Republic">KruÅ¡evo Republic</a>, was crushed with much loss of life.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[70]</a></sup> The uprising and the forming of the KruÅ¡evo Republic are considered the cornerstone and precursors to the eventual establishment of the Macedonian state.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[73]</a></sup> The leaders of the Ilinden uprising are celebrated as national heroes in North Macedonia. The names of IMRO revolutionaries like <a href="/wiki/Gotse_Delchev" title="Gotse Delchev">Gotse Delchev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pitu_Guli" title="Pitu Guli">Pitu Guli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dame_Gruev" title="Dame Gruev">Dame Gruev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yane_Sandanski" title="Yane Sandanski">Yane Sandanski</a> were included into the lyrics of the national anthem of the state of North Macedonia "<a href="/wiki/Denes_nad_Makedonija" title="Denes nad Makedonija">Denes nad Makedonija</a>" ("Today over Macedonia"). The major national holiday of North Macedonia, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_Day_(North_Macedonia)" title="Republic Day (North Macedonia)">Republic Day</a>, is celebrated on 2 August, Ilinden (St. Elijah day), the day of the Ilinden uprising. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Serbia">Kingdom of Serbia</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Second_Balkan_War" title="Second Balkan War">Second Balkan War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbianisation" title="Serbianisation">Serbianisation</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MMTRO_The_Skopie_trial.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/MMTRO_The_Skopie_trial.JPG/220px-MMTRO_The_Skopie_trial.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/MMTRO_The_Skopie_trial.JPG/330px-MMTRO_The_Skopie_trial.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/MMTRO_The_Skopie_trial.JPG/440px-MMTRO_The_Skopie_trial.JPG 2x" data-file-width="901" data-file-height="621"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MMTRO_The_Skopie_trial.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Members of the pro-Bulgarian <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Youth_Secret_Revolutionary_Organization" title="Macedonian Youth Secret Revolutionary Organization">Macedonian Youth Secret Revolutionary Organization</a> (MYSRO) during the <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Student_Trial" title="Skopje Student Trial">Skopje Student Trial</a> in 1927. In December 20 local youths were accused of fighting for an <a href="/wiki/Independent_Macedonia_(IMRO)" title="Independent Macedonia (IMRO)">Independent Macedonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[74]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Following the two <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a> of 1912 and 1913 and the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Dissolution of the Ottoman Empire">dissolution of the Ottoman Empire</a>, most of its European-held territories were divided between Greece, Bulgaria and Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicolle2008162_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicolle2008162-81">[75]</a></sup> The territory that was to become North Macedonia was annexed by Serbia conforming to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Bucharest_(1913)" title="Treaty of Bucharest (1913)">treaty of peace</a> concluded at Bucharest.<sup id="cite_ref-Saucerman_1937_p._195_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saucerman_1937_p._195-82">[76]</a></sup> Following the partition, an anti-Bulgarian campaign was carried out in the areas under Serbian and Greek control.<sup id="cite_ref-Banac_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Banac-83">[77]</a></sup> As many as 641 Bulgarian schools and 761 churches were closed by the Serbs, while Exarchist clergy and teachers were expelled.<sup id="cite_ref-Banac_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Banac-83">[77]</a></sup> The use of all <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_dialects" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedonian dialects">Macedonian dialects</a> and standard Bulgarian were proscribed.<sup id="cite_ref-Banac_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Banac-83">[77]</a></sup> IMRO, together with local Albanians, organised the <a href="/wiki/Ohrid%E2%80%93Debar_uprising" title="OhridâDebar uprising">OhridâDebar uprising</a> against the Serbian rule. Within a few days the rebels captured the towns of Gostivar, Struga and Ohrid, expelling the Serbian troops. According to the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Endowment_for_International_Peace" title="Carnegie Endowment for International Peace">Carnegie Endowment for International Peace</a> report, a Serbian army of 100,000 regulars suppressed the uprising. Many were killed and tens of thousands refugees fled to Bulgaria and Albania.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[79]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Balkan_Wars_Boundaries_cleanup.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Balkan_Wars_Boundaries_cleanup.jpg/220px-Balkan_Wars_Boundaries_cleanup.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="310" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Balkan_Wars_Boundaries_cleanup.jpg/330px-Balkan_Wars_Boundaries_cleanup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Balkan_Wars_Boundaries_cleanup.jpg/440px-Balkan_Wars_Boundaries_cleanup.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1044" data-file-height="1471"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Balkan_Wars_Boundaries_cleanup.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The division of the Ottoman territories in Europe (including the <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(region)" title="Macedonia (region)">region of Macedonia</a>) after the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a> according to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Bucharest_(1913)" title="Treaty of Bucharest (1913)">Treaty of Bucharest</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I">World War I</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_occupation_of_Serbia_(World_War_I)" title="Bulgarian occupation of Serbia (World War I)">Bulgarian occupation of Serbia (World War I)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>, most of today's North Macedonia was part of the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_occupation_of_Serbia_(World_War_I)" title="Bulgarian occupation of Serbia (World War I)">Bulgarian occupied zone of Serbia</a> after the country was <a href="/wiki/Serbian_campaign" title="Serbian campaign">invaded</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> in the fall of 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-Banac_83-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Banac-83">[77]</a></sup> The region was known as the âMilitary Inspection Area of Macedoniaâ and was administered by a Bulgarian military commander.<sup id="cite_ref-KirÃ¡ly_Rothenberg_1985_p.2512_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KirÃ¡ly_Rothenberg_1985_p.2512-86">[80]</a></sup> A policy of <a href="/wiki/Bulgarisation" title="Bulgarisation">Bulgarization</a> of the region and its population was immediately initiated,<sup id="cite_ref-Gerwarth_Horne_2013_p.150_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerwarth_Horne_2013_p.150-87">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bianchi_2012_p.163_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bianchi_2012_p.163-88">[82]</a></sup> during the period the IMRO arose from a clandestine organization to serve as gendarmerie, taking control of the whole police structure, enforcing the Bulgarization of the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Gerwarth_Horne_2013_p.150_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerwarth_Horne_2013_p.150-87">[81]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Robert_Gerwarth" title="Robert Gerwarth">Robert Gerwarth</a>, the Bulgarian denationalization policy, including its paramilitary aspect, was almost identical in its intent and execution to the Serbian policy that preceded it.<sup id="cite_ref-Gerwarth_Horne_2013_p.150_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerwarth_Horne_2013_p.150-87">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bulgarian language was to be exclusively used, <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Serbian Cyrillic alphabet">Serbian cyrillic</a> was forbidden, Serbian priests were arrested and deported, Serbian-sounding names had to be changed to Bulgarian ones,<sup id="cite_ref-Laffan_1989_p.252_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Laffan_1989_p.252-89">[83]</a></sup> schoolteachers were brought from Bulgaria while Serbian books were taken from schools and libraries and publicly destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-Report_of_the_Interallied_Commission_on_the_Violation_of_the_Hague_Convention_p.2_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Report_of_the_Interallied_Commission_on_the_Violation_of_the_Hague_Convention_p.2-90">[84]</a></sup> Adult males were sent to labour camps or forced to join the Bulgarian Army, representatives of the Serbian <a href="/wiki/Intelligentsia" title="Intelligentsia">intelligentsia</a> were deported or executed.<sup id="cite_ref-Bianchi_2012_p.163_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bianchi_2012_p.163-88">[82]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Paul_Mojzes" title="Paul Mojzes">Paul Mojzes</a> the aim of the Bulgarian government was to create pure Bulgarian territories by denationalizing the non-Bulgarian Slavic population of Macedonia.<sup id="cite_ref-Mojzes_2011_p.422_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mojzes_2011_p.422-91">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/South_Serbia_(1919%E2%80%931922)" title="South Serbia (1919â1922)">South Serbia (1919â1922)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vardar_Banovina" title="Vardar Banovina">Vardar Banovina</a>
      </div> 
      <p>After the capitulation of Bulgaria and the end of the First World War, the area returned under Belgrade control as part of the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbs,_Croats_and_Slovenes" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenes">Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenes</a><sup id="cite_ref-NaÅ¡_rod_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NaÅ¡_rod-92">[86]</a></sup> and saw a reintroduction of anti-Bulgarian measures. Bulgarian teachers and clergy were expelled, Bulgarian language signs and books removed, and all Bulgarian organisations dissolved.<sup id="cite_ref-Banac_83-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Banac-83">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Serbian government pursued a policy of forced <a href="/wiki/Serbianisation" title="Serbianisation">Serbianisation</a> in the region,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[88]</a></sup> which included systematic suppression of Bulgarian activists, altering family surnames, internal colonisation, forced labour, and intense propaganda.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[89]</a></sup> To aid the implementation of this policy, some 50,000 Serbian army and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Gendarmerie" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian Gendarmerie">gendarmerie</a> were stationed in present-day North Macedonia.<sup id="cite_ref-Banac_83-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Banac-83">[77]</a></sup> By 1940 about 280 Serbian colonies (comprising 4,200 families) were established as part of the government's internal colonisation program (initial plans envisaged 50,000 families settling in present-day North Macedonia).<sup id="cite_ref-Banac_83-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Banac-83">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1929, the Kingdom was officially renamed the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a>, and divided into provinces called <a href="/wiki/Banovinas_of_the_Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Banovinas of the Kingdom of Yugoslavia"><i>banovinas</i></a>. South Serbia, including all of present-day North Macedonia, became the <a href="/wiki/Vardar_Banovina" title="Vardar Banovina">Vardar Banovina</a> of the Kingdom of Yugoslavia.<sup id="cite_ref-WOW_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WOW-96">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Internal_Macedonian_Revolutionary_Organization" title="Internal Macedonian Revolutionary Organization">Internal Macedonian Revolutionary Organization</a> (IMRO) promoted the concept of an <a href="/wiki/Independent_Macedonia_(IMRO)" title="Independent Macedonia (IMRO)">Independent Macedonia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">interwar period</a>. Its leadersâincluding <a href="/wiki/Todor_Alexandrov" class="mw-redirect" title="Todor Alexandrov">Todor Alexandrov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Protogerov" title="Aleksandar Protogerov">Aleksandar Protogerov</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Mihailov" title="Ivan Mihailov">Ivan Mihailov</a>âpromoted independence of the Macedonian territory split between Serbia and Greece for the whole population, regardless of religion and ethnicity.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[91]</a></sup> The Bulgarian government of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Malinov" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexander Malinov">Alexander Malinov</a> in 1918 offered to give <a href="/wiki/Pirin_Macedonia" title="Pirin Macedonia">Pirin Macedonia</a> for that purpose after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[92]</a></sup> but the Great Powers did not adopt this idea because Serbia and Greece opposed it. In 1924, the <a href="/wiki/Communist_International" title="Communist International">Communist International</a> (Comintern) suggested that all Balkan communist parties adopt a platform of a "<a href="/wiki/United_Macedonia" title="United Macedonia">United Macedonia</a>" but the suggestion was rejected by the Bulgarian and Greek communists.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>IMRO followed by starting an insurgent war in Vardar Macedonia, together with <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Youth_Secret_Revolutionary_Organization" title="Macedonian Youth Secret Revolutionary Organization">Macedonian Youth Secret Revolutionary Organization</a>, which also conducted guerrilla attacks against the Serbian administrative and army officials there. In 1923 in Stip, a paramilitary organisation called <a href="/wiki/Association_against_Bulgarian_Bandits" title="Association against Bulgarian Bandits">Association against Bulgarian Bandits</a> was formed by Serbian <a href="/wiki/Chetniks" title="Chetniks">chetniks</a>, IMRO renegades and <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Federative_Organization" title="Macedonian Federative Organization">Macedonian Federative Organization</a> (MFO) members to oppose IMRO and MMTRO.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[94]</a></sup> On 9 October 1934 IMRO member <a href="/wiki/Vlado_Chernozemski" title="Vlado Chernozemski">Vlado Chernozemski</a> assassinated <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Yugoslavia" title="Alexander I of Yugoslavia">Alexander I of Yugoslavia</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Macedonism" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedonism">Macedonist</a> ideas increased in Yugoslav Vardar Macedonia and among the left diaspora in Bulgaria during the interwar period. They were supported by the Comintern.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-101">[95]</a></sup> In 1934, the Comintern issued a <a href="/wiki/Resolution_of_the_Comintern_on_the_Macedonian_question" title="Resolution of the Comintern on the Macedonian question">special resolution</a> in which for the first time directions were provided for recognising the existence of a separate Macedonian nation and Macedonian language.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_in_Yugoslav_Macedonia" title="World War II in Yugoslav Macedonia">World War II in Yugoslav Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Liberation_of_Skopje.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7e/Liberation_of_Skopje.jpg/220px-Liberation_of_Skopje.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7e/Liberation_of_Skopje.jpg/330px-Liberation_of_Skopje.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/7e/Liberation_of_Skopje.jpg 2x" data-file-width="386" data-file-height="258"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Liberation_of_Skopje.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Dimitar_Vlahov" title="Dimitar Vlahov">Dimitar Vlahov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mihajlo_Apostolski" class="mw-redirect" title="Mihajlo Apostolski">Mihajlo Apostolski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metodija_Andonov-%C4%8Cento" title="Metodija Andonov-Äento">Metodija Andonov-Äento</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lazar_Koli%C5%A1evski" title="Lazar KoliÅ¡evski">Lazar KoliÅ¡evski</a> and others, greeted in Skopje on 20 November 1944, a week after its liberation<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[97]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During World War II, Yugoslavia was occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a> from 1941 to 1945. The Vardar Banovina was divided between Bulgaria and Italian-occupied Albania. <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Action_Committees" title="Bulgarian Action Committees">Bulgarian Action Committees</a> were established to prepare the region for the new Bulgarian administration and army.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[98]</a></sup> The committees were mostly formed by former members of IMRO and <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Youth_Secret_Revolutionary_Organization" title="Macedonian Youth Secret Revolutionary Organization">Macedonian Youth Secret Revolutionary Organization</a> (MYSRO, but some <a href="/wiki/IMRO_(United)" class="mw-redirect" title="IMRO (United)">IMRO (United)</a> former members also participated.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorgievaKonechni1998223_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorgievaKonechni1998223-106">[100]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As leader of the Vardar Macedonian communists, <a href="/wiki/Metodi_Shatorov" title="Metodi Shatorov">Metodi Shatorov</a> ("Sharlo") switched from the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Communist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Yugoslav Communist Party">Yugoslav Communist Party</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Communist_Party" title="Bulgarian Communist Party">Bulgarian Communist Party</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorgievaKonechni1998223_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorgievaKonechni1998223-106">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[101]</a></sup> and refused to start military action against the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian Army">Bulgarian Army</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[102]</a></sup> The Bulgarian authorities, under German pressure,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[103]</a></sup> were responsible for the round-up and deportation of over 7,000 Jews in Skopje and <a href="/wiki/Bitola" title="Bitola">Bitola</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[104]</a></sup> Harsh rule by the occupying forces encouraged many Vardar Macedonians to support the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Partisans" title="Yugoslav Partisans">Communist Partisan</a> resistance movement of <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a> after 1943,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[g]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_War_of_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="National Liberation War of Macedonia">National Liberation War</a> ensued.<sup id="cite_ref-ÐÐÐ_Ð½Ð°_ÐÐ°ÐºÐµÐ´Ð¾Ð½Ð¸ÑÐ°_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ÐÐÐ_Ð½Ð°_ÐÐ°ÐºÐµÐ´Ð¾Ð½Ð¸ÑÐ°-112">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ÐÑÑÐ¾ÑÐ¸ÑÐ°_Ð½Ð°_ÐÐ_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ÐÑÑÐ¾ÑÐ¸ÑÐ°_Ð½Ð°_ÐÐ-113">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Vardar Macedonia, after the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_of_1944" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian coup d'Ã©tat of 1944">Bulgarian coup d'Ã©tat of 1944</a>, the Bulgarian troops, surrounded by German forces, fought their way back to the old borders of Bulgaria.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[107]</a></sup> Under the leadership of the new Bulgarian pro-Soviet government, four armies, 455,000 strong in total, were mobilised and reorganised. Most of them re-entered occupied Yugoslavia in early October 1944 and moved from <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a> to <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%A1" title="NiÅ¡">NiÅ¡</a>, Skopje and <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> with the strategic task of blocking the German forces withdrawing from Greece.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[108]</a></sup> The Bulgarian army would <a href="/wiki/Nagykanizsa%E2%80%93K%C3%B6rmend_Offensive" title="NagykanizsaâKÃ¶rmend Offensive">reach the Alps</a> in Austria, participating in the expulsion of the Germans to the west, through Yugoslavia and Hungary. </p>
      <p>Compelled by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> with a view towards the creation of a large <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavism" title="Yugoslavism">South Slav Federation</a>, in 1946 the new Communist government, led by <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Dimitrov" title="Georgi Dimitrov">Georgi Dimitrov</a>, agreed to give Bulgarian Macedonia to a <a href="/wiki/United_Macedonia" title="United Macedonia">United Macedonia</a>. With the <a href="/wiki/Bled_agreement_(1947)" title="Bled agreement (1947)">Bled agreement</a>, in 1947 Bulgaria formally confirmed the envisioned unification of the Macedonian region, but postponed this act until after the formation of the future Federation.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[110]</a></sup> It was the first time it accepted the existence of a separate Macedonian ethnicity and language. After the <a href="/wiki/Tito%E2%80%93Stalin_split" title="TitoâStalin split">TitoâStalin split</a> the region of Pirin Macedonia remained part of Bulgaria and later the Bulgarian Communist Party revised its view of existence of a separate Macedonian nation and language. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Socialist_Yugoslavia">Socialist Yugoslavia</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Socialist Republic of Macedonia">Socialist Republic of Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lazar_Kolishevski_left.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Lazar_Kolishevski_left.jpg/160px-Lazar_Kolishevski_left.jpg" decoding="async" width="160" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Lazar_Kolishevski_left.jpg/240px-Lazar_Kolishevski_left.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Lazar_Kolishevski_left.jpg/320px-Lazar_Kolishevski_left.jpg 2x" data-file-width="644" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lazar_Kolishevski_left.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Lazar_Koli%C5%A1evski" title="Lazar KoliÅ¡evski">Lazar KoliÅ¡evski</a> was the political leader of SR Macedonia and briefly of SFR Yugoslavia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In December 1944 the <a href="/wiki/Anti-fascist_Assembly_for_the_National_Liberation_of_Macedonia" title="Anti-fascist Assembly for the National Liberation of Macedonia">Anti-fascist Assembly for the National Liberation of Macedonia</a> (ASNOM) proclaimed the People's Republic of Macedonia as part of the <i>People's Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[111]</a></sup> ASNOM remained an acting government until the end of the war. The Macedonian alphabet was codified by linguists of ASNOM, who based their alphabet on the phonetic alphabet of <a href="/wiki/Vuk_Stefanovi%C4%87_Karad%C5%BEi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Vuk StefanoviÄ KaradÅ¾iÄ">Vuk StefanoviÄ KaradÅ¾iÄ</a> and the principles of <a href="/wiki/Krste_Misirkov" title="Krste Misirkov">Krste Petkov Misirkov</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Civil_War" title="Greek Civil War">civil war in Greece</a> (1946â1949), Macedonian communist insurgents supported the Greek communists. Many refugees fled to the Socialist Republic of Macedonia from there. The state dropped <i>Socialist</i> from its name in 1991 when it peacefully seceded from Yugoslavia. </p>
      <p>The new republic became one of the six republics of the Yugoslav federation. Following the federation's renaming as the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a> in 1963, the People's Republic of Macedonia was likewise renamed the Socialist Republic of Macedonia.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[114]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Declaration_of_independence">Declaration of independence</span></h4> 
      <p>North Macedonia officially celebrates 8 September 1991 as <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(North_Macedonia)" title="Independence Day (North Macedonia)">Independence day</a> (<a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">ÐÐµÐ½ Ð½Ð° Ð½ÐµÐ·Ð°Ð²Ð¸ÑÐ½Ð¾ÑÑÐ°</span>, <i>Den na nezavisnosta</i>), with regard to <a href="/wiki/1991_Macedonian_independence_referendum" title="1991 Macedonian independence referendum">the referendum endorsing independence from Yugoslavia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NS_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NS-122">[115]</a></sup> The anniversary of the start of the <a href="/wiki/Ilinden%E2%80%93Preobrazhenie_Uprising" title="IlindenâPreobrazhenie Uprising">Ilinden Uprising</a> (<a href="/wiki/Elijah" title="Elijah">St. Elijah</a>'s Day) on 2 August is also widely celebrated on an official level as the <a href="/wiki/Republic_Day_(North_Macedonia)" title="Republic Day (North Macedonia)">Day of the Republic</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Robert_Badinter" title="Robert Badinter">Robert Badinter</a>, as the head of the <a href="/wiki/Arbitration_Commission_of_the_Peace_Conference_on_Yugoslavia" title="Arbitration Commission of the Peace Conference on Yugoslavia">Arbitration Commission of the Peace Conference on Yugoslavia</a>, recommended EC recognition in January 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Macedonia remained at peace through the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">Yugoslav Wars</a> of the early 1990s. A few very minor changes to its border with Yugoslavia were agreed upon to resolve problems with the demarcation line between the two countries. It was seriously destabilised by the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a> in 1999, when an estimated 360,000 ethnic Albanian refugees from Kosovo took refuge in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Thomas_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas-124">[117]</a></sup> They departed shortly after the war, and <a href="/wiki/Albanian_nationalism" title="Albanian nationalism">Albanian nationalists</a> on both sides of the border took up arms soon after in pursuit of autonomy or independence for the Albanian-populated areas of Macedonia.<sup id="cite_ref-Thomas_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas-124">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-125">[118]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2001_insurgency">2001 insurgency</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/2001_insurgency_in_Macedonia" title="2001 insurgency in Macedonia">2001 insurgency in Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Albanian_Protesters_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Albanian_Protesters_2.jpg/220px-Albanian_Protesters_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Albanian_Protesters_2.jpg/330px-Albanian_Protesters_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Albanian_Protesters_2.jpg/440px-Albanian_Protesters_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="799" data-file-height="533"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Albanian_Protesters_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/2012_Republic_of_Macedonia_inter-ethnic_violence" title="2012 Republic of Macedonia inter-ethnic violence">inter-ethnic violence</a> in present-day North Macedonia in 2012
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/2001_insurgency_in_Macedonia" title="2001 insurgency in Macedonia">conflict</a> took place between the government and ethnic Albanian insurgents, mostly in the north and west of the country, between February and August 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-125">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stat.gov.mk2_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat.gov.mk2-126">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[120]</a></sup> The war ended with the intervention of a <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> ceasefire monitoring force. Under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Ohrid_Agreement" title="Ohrid Agreement">Ohrid Agreement</a>, the government agreed to devolve greater political power and cultural recognition to the Albanian minority.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[121]</a></sup> The Albanian side agreed to abandon separatist demands and to recognise all Macedonian institutions fully. In addition, according to this accord, the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Army_(North_Macedonia)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Liberation Army (North Macedonia)">NLA</a> were to disarm and hand over their weapons to a NATO force.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[122]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/2012_Republic_of_Macedonia_inter-ethnic_violence" title="2012 Republic of Macedonia inter-ethnic violence">Inter-ethnic tensions</a> flared in Macedonia in 2012, with incidents of violence between ethnic Albanians and Macedonians.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[123]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquisation">Antiquisation</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Antiquization" title="Antiquization">Antiquization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macedonism" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedonism">Macedonism</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Upon the coming to power in 2006, but especially since the country's non-invitation to NATO in 2008, the VMRO-DPMNE government pursued a policy of "<a href="/wiki/Macedonian_nationalism#Post-independence_period_and_Antiquisation" title="Macedonian nationalism">Antiquisation</a>" ("Antikvizatzija") as a way of putting pressure on Greece as well as for the purposes of domestic identity-building.<sup id="cite_ref-Georgievski_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Georgievski-131">[124]</a></sup> Statues of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Macedon" title="Philip II of Macedon">Philip of Macedon</a> have been built in several cities across the country. Additionally, many pieces of public infrastructure, such as airports, highways, and stadiums were renamed after Alexander and Philip. These actions were seen as deliberate provocations in neighbouring Greece, exacerbating the dispute and further stalling the country's EU and NATO applications.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[125]</a></sup> The policy has also attracted criticism domestically, as well as from EU diplomats,<sup id="cite_ref-Georgievski_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Georgievski-131">[124]</a></sup> and, following the Prespa agreement, it has been partly reversed after 2016 by the new <a href="/wiki/SDSM" class="mw-redirect" title="SDSM">SDSM</a> government of North Macedonia.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[127]</a></sup> Moreover, per Prespa agreement both countries have acknowledged that their respective understanding of the terms "Macedonia" and "Macedonian" refers to a different historical context and cultural heritage. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="EU_and_NATO_path">EU and NATO path</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_naming_dispute" title="Macedonia naming dispute">Macedonia naming dispute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prespa_agreement" title="Prespa agreement">Prespa agreement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_North_Macedonia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of North Macedonia to the European Union">Accession of North Macedonia to the European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia%E2%80%93NATO_relations" title="North MacedoniaâNATO relations">North MacedoniaâNATO relations</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria%E2%80%93North_Macedonia_relations" title="BulgariaâNorth Macedonia relations">BulgariaâNorth Macedonia relations</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%83%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%9A%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%B3%D1%80%D1%87%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%82_%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80_(17.06.2018,_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B0)_(42853677381).jpg"
