decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/%D0%9F%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%83%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%9A%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%B3%D1%80%D1%87%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%82_%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80_%2817.06.2018%2C_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B0%29_%2842853677381%29.jpg/330px-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%83%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%9A%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%B3%D1%80%D1%87%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%82_%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80_%2817.06.2018%2C_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B0%29_%2842853677381%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/%D0%9F%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%83%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%9A%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%B3%D1%80%D1%87%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%82_%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80_%2817.06.2018%2C_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B0%29_%2842853677381%29.jpg/440px-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%83%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%9A%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%B3%D1%80%D1%87%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%82_%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80_%2817.06.2018%2C_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B0%29_%2842853677381%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3280"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%83%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%9A%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%B3%D1%80%D1%87%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%82_%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80_(17.06.2018,_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B0)_(42853677381).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Symbolic signing of the Prespa agreement
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Prespa_agreement" title="Prespa agreement">Prespa agreement</a>, which replaces the Interim Accord of 1995,<sup id="cite_ref-2018FinalAgreement_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018FinalAgreement-135">[128]</a></sup> was signed on 17 June 2018 by the two foreign ministers <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Dimitrov" title="Nikola Dimitrov">Nikola Dimitrov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nikos_Kotzias" title="Nikos Kotzias">Nikos Kotzias</a> and in the presence of the respective prime ministers, <a href="/wiki/Zoran_Zaev" title="Zoran Zaev">Zoran Zaev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Tsipras" title="Alexis Tsipras">Alexis Tsipras</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[129]</a></sup> The Prespa agreement was preceded by signing <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria%E2%80%93North_Macedonia_relations#The_Friendship_treaty_and_beyond" title="BulgariaâNorth Macedonia relations">Friendship agreement</a> with Bulgaria in August 2017, aiming to end the "anti-Bulgarian ideology" in North Macedonia and to solve the historical issues between the two counties. </p>
      <p>The withdrawal of the Greek veto, along with the signing the Friendship agreement with Bulgaria, resulted in the European Union on 27 June approving the start of <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_North_Macedonia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of North Macedonia to the European Union">accession talks</a>, which were expected to take place in 2019, under the condition that the Prespa deal was implemented and the country's name was changed to <i>Republic of North Macedonia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[130]</a></sup> On 5 July, the Prespa agreement was ratified again by the Macedonian parliament with 69 MPs voting in favour of it.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[131]</a></sup> On 12 July, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> invited Macedonia to start accession talks in a bid to become the EuroAtlantic alliance's 30th member.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[132]</a></sup> On 30 July, the parliament of Macedonia approved plans to hold a non-binding <a href="/wiki/2018_Macedonian_referendum" title="2018 Macedonian referendum">referendum on changing the country's name</a>, which took place on 30 September.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[133]</a></sup> Ninety-one percent of voters voted in favour with a 37% turnout,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[134]</a></sup> but the referendum was not carried because of a constitutional requirement for a 50% turnout.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[135]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:North_Macedonia_Joins_NATO.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/North_Macedonia_Joins_NATO.jpg/220px-North_Macedonia_Joins_NATO.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/North_Macedonia_Joins_NATO.jpg/330px-North_Macedonia_Joins_NATO.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/North_Macedonia_Joins_NATO.jpg/440px-North_Macedonia_Joins_NATO.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6783" data-file-height="4845"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:North_Macedonia_Joins_NATO.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>North Macedonia commemorates its accession to NATO at the US Department of State.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 6 February 2019, the permanent representatives of NATO member states and Macedonian Foreign Affairs Minister Nikola Dimitrov, signed in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> the <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_North_Macedonia_to_NATO" class="mw-redirect" title="Accession of North Macedonia to NATO">accession protocol</a> of North Macedonia into NATO.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[137]</a></sup> The protocol was then ratified on 8 February by the Greek parliament, thus completing all the preconditions for putting into force the Prespa agreement. Subsequently, on 12 February the Macedonian government announced the formal activation of the constitutional amendments which effectively renamed the country as North Macedonia and informed accordingly the United Nations and its member states.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In March 2020, after the ratification process by all NATO members was completed, North Macedonia <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia%E2%80%93NATO_relations" title="North MacedoniaâNATO relations">acceded to NATO</a>, becoming the 30th member state.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[141]</a></sup> The same month, the leaders of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> formally gave approval to North Macedonia begin talks to join the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[143]</a></sup> On November 17, 2020, Bulgaria has refused to approve the European Union's negotiation framework for North Macedonia, effectively blocking the official start of accession talks with this country.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[144]</a></sup> The explanation from Bulgarian side was: no implementation of the Friendship treaty from 2017, state-supported hate speech, minority claims, and an 'ongoing nation-building process' based on historical negationism of the Bulgarian identity, culture and legacy in the broader <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(region)" title="Macedonia (region)">region of Macedonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[145]</a></sup> The veto received condemnation by intellectuals from both states<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[146]</a></sup> and criticism from international observers.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[148]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_North_Macedonia" title="Geography of North Macedonia">Geography of North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location">Location</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mount_Korab,_Republic_of_Macedonia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Mount_Korab%2C_Republic_of_Macedonia.jpg/220px-Mount_Korab%2C_Republic_of_Macedonia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Mount_Korab%2C_Republic_of_Macedonia.jpg/330px-Mount_Korab%2C_Republic_of_Macedonia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Mount_Korab%2C_Republic_of_Macedonia.jpg/440px-Mount_Korab%2C_Republic_of_Macedonia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mount_Korab,_Republic_of_Macedonia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mount_Korab" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Korab">Mount Korab</a>, the highest mountain in North Macedonia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>North Macedonia has a total area of 25,713&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (9,928&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/40th_parallel_north" title="40th parallel north">40Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/43rd_parallel_north" title="43rd parallel north">43Â° N</a>, and mostly between longitudes <a href="/wiki/20th_meridian_east" title="20th meridian east">20Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/23rd_meridian_east" title="23rd meridian east">23Â° E</a> (a small area lies east of 23Â°). North Macedonia has some 748&nbsp;km (465&nbsp;mi) of boundaries, shared with <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> (62&nbsp;km or 39&nbsp;mi) to the North, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> (159&nbsp;km or 99&nbsp;mi) to the northwest, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> (148&nbsp;km or 92&nbsp;mi) to the east, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> (228&nbsp;km or 142&nbsp;mi) to the south, and <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> (151&nbsp;km or 94&nbsp;mi) to the west. It is a transit way for shipment of goods from Greece, through the Balkans, towards Eastern, Western and Central Europe and through Bulgaria to the east. It is part of the larger region of <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(region)" title="Macedonia (region)">Macedonia</a>, which also includes <a href="/wiki/Greek_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Macedonia">Greek Macedonia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Blagoevgrad_Province" title="Blagoevgrad Province">Blagoevgrad Province</a> in southwestern Bulgaria. </p>
      <p>North Macedonia is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> that is geographically clearly defined by a central valley formed by the Vardar river and framed along its borders by mountain ranges. The terrain is mostly rugged, located between the <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ar_Mountains" title="Å ar Mountains">Å ar Mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Osogovo" title="Osogovo">Osogovo</a>, which frame the valley of the <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar</a> river. Three large lakesâ<a href="/wiki/Lake_Ohrid" title="Lake Ohrid">Lake Ohrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Prespa" title="Lake Prespa">Lake Prespa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dojran_Lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Dojran Lake">Dojran Lake</a>âlie on the southern borders, bisected by the frontiers with Albania and Greece. Ohrid is considered to be one of the oldest lakes and biotopes in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[149]</a></sup> The region is seismically active and has been the site of destructive earthquakes in the past, most recently in 1963 when Skopje was heavily damaged by a major earthquake, killing over 1,000. </p>
      <p>North Macedonia also has scenic mountains. They belong to two different mountain ranges: the first is the Å ar Mountains<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[151]</a></sup> that continues to the West Vardar/Pelagonia group of mountains (<a href="/wiki/Baba_Mountain,_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Baba Mountain, Macedonia">Baba Mountain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nid%C5%BEe" class="mw-redirect" title="NidÅ¾e">NidÅ¾e</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%BEuf" title="KoÅ¾uf">Kozuf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jakupica" title="Jakupica">Jakupica</a>), also known as the <a href="/wiki/Dinaric_Alps" title="Dinaric Alps">Dinaric range</a>. The second range is the <a href="/wiki/Osogovo" title="Osogovo">Osogovo</a>â<a href="/wiki/Belasica" title="Belasica">Belasica</a> mountain chain, also known as the <a href="/wiki/Rhodope_Mountains" title="Rhodope Mountains">Rhodope range</a>. The mountains belonging to the Å ar Mountains and the West Vardar/Pelagonia range are younger and higher than the older mountains of the Osogovo-Belasica mountain group. <a href="/wiki/Mount_Korab" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Korab">Mount Korab</a> of the Å ar Mountains on the Albanian border, at 2,764&nbsp;m (9,068&nbsp;ft), is the tallest mountain in North Macedonia. In North Macedonia there are 1,100 large sources of water. The rivers flow into three different basins: the Aegean, the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[152]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Matka_Lake_-_Macedonia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Matka_Lake_-_Macedonia.jpg/220px-Matka_Lake_-_Macedonia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Matka_Lake_-_Macedonia.jpg/330px-Matka_Lake_-_Macedonia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Matka_Lake_-_Macedonia.jpg/440px-Matka_Lake_-_Macedonia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Matka_Lake_-_Macedonia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Matka_Canyon" title="Matka Canyon">Matka Canyon</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Aegean basin is the largest. It covers 87% of the territory of North Macedonia, which is 22,075 square kilometres (8,523&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar</a>, the largest river in this basin, drains 80% of the territory or 20,459 square kilometres (7,899&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). Its valley plays an important part in the economy and the communication system of the country. The Vardar Valley project is considered to be crucial for the strategic development of the country. The river <a href="/wiki/Black_Drin" title="Black Drin">Black Drin</a> forms the Adriatic basin, which covers an area of about 3,320&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (1,282&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), i.e., 13% of the territory. It receives water from Lakes Prespa and Ohrid. The Black Sea basin is the smallest with only 37&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (14&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). It covers the northern side of Mount <a href="/wiki/Skopska_Crna_Gora" title="Skopska Crna Gora">Skopska Crna Gora</a>. This is the source of the river Binachka Morava, which joins the <a href="/wiki/Great_Morava" title="Great Morava">Morava</a>, and later, the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>, which flows into the Black Sea. North Macedonia has around fifty ponds and three natural lakes, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ohrid" title="Lake Ohrid">Lake Ohrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Prespa" title="Lake Prespa">Lake Prespa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Dojran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lake Dojran">Lake Dojran</a>. In North Macedonia there are nine spa towns and resorts: BaniÅ¡te, Banja Bansko, Istibanja, Katlanovo, <a href="/wiki/Ke%C5%BEovica" title="KeÅ¾ovica">KeÅ¾ovica</a>, Kosovrasti, Banja KoÄani, Kumanovski Banji and Negorci. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_North_Macedonia#Climate" title="Geography of North Macedonia">Climate of North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_MKD_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Koppen-Geiger_Map_MKD_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_MKD_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Koppen-Geiger_Map_MKD_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_MKD_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Koppen-Geiger_Map_MKD_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_MKD_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1754" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_MKD_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen%E2%80%93Geiger" class="mw-redirect" title="KÃ¶ppenâGeiger">KÃ¶ppenâGeiger</a> climate classification map for North Macedonia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Four different seasons are found in the country with warm and dry summers and moderately cold and snowy winters. The range of temperatures recorded throughout the year ranges from â20&nbsp;Â°C (â4&nbsp;Â°F) in winter, to 40&nbsp;Â°C (104&nbsp;Â°F) in summer. Low winter temperatures are influenced by winds from the north while heat seasons during summer arise due to the subtropical pressure of the Aegean Sea and climate influences from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, with the latter causing dry periods.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorgievaKonechni199873_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorgievaKonechni199873-160">[153]</a></sup> There are three main climatic zones in the country: mildly <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental</a> in the north, temperate <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean</a> in the south and <a href="/wiki/Mountain_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain climate">mountainous</a> in the zones with high altitude.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorgievaKonechni199831_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorgievaKonechni199831-161">[154]</a></sup> Along the valleys of the Vardar and Strumica rivers, in the regions of <a href="/wiki/Gevgelija" title="Gevgelija">Gevgelija</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valandovo" title="Valandovo">Valandovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dojran" title="Dojran">Dojran</a>, Strumica, and <a href="/wiki/Radovi%C5%A1" title="RadoviÅ¡">RadoviÅ¡</a>, the climate is temperate Mediterranean. The warmest regions are <a href="/wiki/Demir_Kapija" title="Demir Kapija">Demir Kapija</a> and Gevgelija, where the temperature in July and August frequently exceeds 40&nbsp;Â°C (104&nbsp;Â°F).<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[155]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Average annual precipitation varies from 1,700&nbsp;mm (66.9&nbsp;in) in the western mountainous area to 500&nbsp;mm (19.7&nbsp;in) in the eastern area. There is a low level of precipitation in the Vardar valley with 500&nbsp;mm (19.7&nbsp;in) of water per year.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorgievaKonechni199873_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorgievaKonechni199873-160">[153]</a></sup> The climate and irrigation diversity allow the cultivation of different plant types, including <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corn" class="mw-redirect" title="Corn">corn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potatoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Potatoes">potatoes</a>, poppies, peanuts, and <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorgievaKonechni19982_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorgievaKonechni19982-163">[156]</a></sup> There are thirty main and regular weather stations in the country. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_North_Macedonia" title="Wildlife of North Macedonia">Wildlife of North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:174px;max-width:174px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:172px;max-width:172px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Lynx_lynx_poing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Lynx_lynx_poing.jpg/170px-Lynx_lynx_poing.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Lynx_lynx_poing.jpg/255px-Lynx_lynx_poing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Lynx_lynx_poing.jpg/340px-Lynx_lynx_poing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="533" data-file-height="800"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_lynx" title="Eurasian lynx">Eurasian lynx</a>.
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:172px;max-width:172px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Sarplaninac_front.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Sarplaninac_front.jpg/170px-Sarplaninac_front.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5b/Sarplaninac_front.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="300"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0arplaninac" title="Å arplaninac">Å arplaninec</a>.
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The flora of North Macedonia is represented by around 210 <a href="/wiki/Family_(biology)" title="Family (biology)">families</a>, 920 <a href="/wiki/Genus_(biology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Genus (biology)">genera</a>, and around 3,700 plant species. The most abundant group are the <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">flowering plants</a> with around 3,200 species, followed by <a href="/wiki/Moss" title="Moss">mosses</a> (350 species) and <a href="/wiki/Fern" title="Fern">ferns</a> (42). </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, North Macedonia belongs to the Illyrian province of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">World Wide Fund for Nature</a> (WWF) and the Digital Map of European Ecological Regions by the <a href="/wiki/European_Environment_Agency" title="European Environment Agency">European Environment Agency</a>, the territory of the Republic can be subdivided into four terrestrial <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregions</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Pindus_Mountains_mixed_forests" title="Pindus Mountains mixed forests">Pindus Mountains mixed forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balkan_mixed_forests" title="Balkan mixed forests">Balkan mixed forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rodope_montane_mixed_forests" title="Rodope montane mixed forests">Rodope montane mixed forests</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aegean_and_Western_Turkey_sclerophyllous_and_mixed_forests" title="Aegean and Western Turkey sclerophyllous and mixed forests">Aegean and Western Turkey sclerophyllous and mixed forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-164">[157]</a></sup> North Macedonia had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 7.42/10, ranking it 40<sup>th</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-165">[158]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Baba_Mountain,_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Baba Mountain, Macedonia">National Park of Pelister</a> in Bitola is known for the presence of the endemic <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Pine" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedonian Pine">Macedonian Pine</a>, as well as some 88 species of plants representing almost 30 percent of North Macedonian dendroflora. The Macedonian Pine forests on Pelister are divided into two communities: pine forests with ferns and pine forests with junipers. The Macedonian Pine, as a specific conifer species, is a <a href="/wiki/Relict" title="Relict">relict</a> of tertiary flora, and the five-needle pine <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Pine" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedonian Pine">Molika</a>, was first noted on Pelister in 1893. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pelister_Molika.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Pelister_Molika.jpg/220px-Pelister_Molika.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Pelister_Molika.jpg/330px-Pelister_Molika.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Pelister_Molika.jpg/440px-Pelister_Molika.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="2560"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pelister_Molika.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Pinus_peuce" title="Pinus peuce">Pinus peuce</a></i>, the Macedonian Pine or Molika, one of North Macedonia's most recognisable trees
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>North Macedonia's limited forest growth also includes <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Oak" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedonian Oak">Macedonian Oaks</a>, the sycamore, weeping willows, white willows, alders, poplars, elms, and the common ash. Near the rich pastures on Å ar Mountain and Bistra, Mavrovo, is another plant species characteristic of plant life in Macedoniaâthe <a href="/wiki/Poppy" title="Poppy">poppy</a>. The quality of thick poppy juice is measured worldwide by morphine units; while Chinese <a href="/wiki/Opium" title="Opium">opium</a> contains eight such units and is considered to be of high quality, Indian opium contains seven units, and Turkish opium only six, Macedonian opium contains a full 14 morphine units and is one of the best quality opiums in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[159]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The native forest fauna is abundant and includes bears, <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boars</a>, wolves, foxes, squirrels, <a href="/wiki/Chamois" title="Chamois">chamois</a> and deer. The <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_lynx" title="Eurasian lynx">lynx</a> is found, very rarely, in the mountains of western Macedonia, while deer can be found in the region of <a href="/wiki/Demir_Kapija" title="Demir Kapija">Demir Kapija</a>. Forest birds include the <a href="/wiki/Blackcap" class="mw-redirect" title="Blackcap">blackcap</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Grouse" title="Grouse">grouse</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Black_grouse" title="Black grouse">black grouse</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_imperial_eagle" title="Eastern imperial eagle">imperial eagle</a> and the forest owl. </p>
      <p>The country has three <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national parks</a>: </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
