      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_North_Macedonia" title="Politics of North Macedonia">Politics of North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_-_Parlamentsgeb%C3%A4ude_der_Republik_Mazedonien.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Skopje_-_Parlamentsgeb%C3%A4ude_der_Republik_Mazedonien.jpg/220px-Skopje_-_Parlamentsgeb%C3%A4ude_der_Republik_Mazedonien.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Skopje_-_Parlamentsgeb%C3%A4ude_der_Republik_Mazedonien.jpg/330px-Skopje_-_Parlamentsgeb%C3%A4ude_der_Republik_Mazedonien.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Skopje_-_Parlamentsgeb%C3%A4ude_der_Republik_Mazedonien.jpg/440px-Skopje_-_Parlamentsgeb%C3%A4ude_der_Republik_Mazedonien.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4465" data-file-height="3328"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_-_Parlamentsgeb%C3%A4ude_der_Republik_Mazedonien.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_North_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliament of North Macedonia">Parliament Building of North Macedonia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Skopje" title="Skopje">Skopje</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>North Macedonia is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary democracy</a> with an <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive government</a> composed of a coalition of parties from the <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral legislature</a> (<span lang="mk" title="Macedonian-language text">Ð¡Ð¾Ð±ÑÐ°Ð½Ð¸Ðµ</span>, <i lang="mk-Latn" title="Macedonian-language text">Sobranie</i>) and an independent <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judicial branch</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_court" title="Constitutional court">constitutional court</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_North_Macedonia" title="Assembly of North Macedonia">Assembly</a> is made up of 120 seats and the members are elected every four years. The role of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_North_Macedonia" title="President of North Macedonia">President</a> is mostly ceremonial, with the real power resting in the hands of the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_North_Macedonia" title="Prime Minister of North Macedonia">Prime Minister</a>. The President is the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the state armed forces and a president of the <a href="/wiki/National_security" title="National security">state Security</a> Council. The President is elected every five years and he or she can be elected twice at most. </p>
      <p>With the passage of a new law and elections held in 2005, local government functions are divided between 78 <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_North_Macedonia" title="Municipalities of North Macedonia">municipalities</a> (<span lang="mk" title="Macedonian-language text">Ð¾Ð¿ÑÑÐ¸Ð½Ð¸</span>, <i lang="mk-Latn" title="Macedonian-language text">opÅ¡tini</i>; <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">singular</a>: <span lang="mk" title="Macedonian-language text">Ð¾Ð¿ÑÑÐ¸Ð½Ð°</span>, <i lang="mk-Latn" title="Macedonian-language text">opÅ¡tina</i>). The capital, Skopje, is governed as a group of ten municipalities collectively referred to as the "City of Skopje". Municipalities in North Macedonia are units of local self-government. Neighbouring municipalities may establish co-operative arrangements. </p>
      <p>The country's main political divergence is between the largely ethnically based political parties representing the country's ethnic Macedonian majority and Albanian minority. The issue of the power balance between the two communities led to a brief war in 2001, following which a power-sharing agreement was reached. In August 2004, parliament passed legislation redrawing local boundaries and giving greater local autonomy to ethnic Albanians in areas where they predominate. </p>
      <p>After a troublesome pre-election campaign, North Macedonia saw a relatively calm and democratic change of government in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Macedonian_parliamentary_election" title="2006 Macedonian parliamentary election">elections held on 5 July 2006</a>. The elections were marked by a decisive victory of the centre-right party <a href="/wiki/VMRO%E2%80%93DPMNE" class="mw-redirect" title="VMROâDPMNE">VMRO-DPMNE</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Gruevski" title="Nikola Gruevski">Nikola Gruevski</a>. Gruevski's decision to include the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Albanians" title="Democratic Party of Albanians">Democratic Party of Albanians</a> in the new government, instead of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Union_for_Integration" title="Democratic Union for Integration">Democratic Union for Integration</a>â<a href="/wiki/Party_for_Democratic_Prosperity" title="Party for Democratic Prosperity">Party for Democratic Prosperity</a> coalition which won the majority of the Albanian votes, triggered protests throughout the parts of the country with a respective number of Albanian population. A dialogue was later established between the Democratic Union for Integration and the ruling VMRO-DMPNE party as an effort to talk about the disputes between the two parties and to support European and NATO aspirations of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[160]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the early parliamentary elections held in 2008, VMRO-DPMNE and Democratic Union for Integration formed a ruling coalition.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[161]</a></sup> In April 2009, presidential and local elections in the country were carried out peacefully, which was crucial for Macedonian aspirations to join the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[162]</a></sup> The ruling conservative VMRO-DPMNE party won a victory in the local elections and the candidate supported by the party, Gjorgi Ivanov, was elected as the new president. </p>
      <p>As of 4&nbsp;January&nbsp;2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=North_Macedonia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the acting Prime Minister of North Macedonia is <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Spasovski" title="Oliver Spasovski">Oliver Spasovski</a> and the current President of the Parliament is <a href="/wiki/Talat_Xhaferi" title="Talat Xhaferi">Talat Xhaferi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-xhaferi_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xhaferi-170">[163]</a></sup> The election of Xhaferi was immediately met with protests led by VMRO-DPMNE, which was quickly handled by the police.<sup id="cite_ref-xhaferi_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xhaferi-170">[163]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Parliament, or <i>Sobranie</i> (<a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">Ð¡Ð¾Ð±ÑÐ°Ð½Ð¸Ðµ</span>), is the country's legislative body. It makes, proposes and adopts laws. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_North_Macedonia" title="Constitution of North Macedonia">Constitution of North Macedonia</a> has been in use since the formation of the republic in the 1993. It limits the power of the governments, both local and national. The military is also limited by the constitution. The constitution states that North Macedonia is a social free state, and that Skopje is the capital.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[164]</a></sup> The 120 members are elected for a mandate of four years through a general election. Each citizen aged 18&nbsp;years or older can vote for one of the political parties. The current president of Parliament is <a href="/wiki/Talat_Xhaferi" title="Talat Xhaferi">Talat Xhaferi</a>. </p>
      <p>Executive power in North Macedonia is exercised by the Government, whose prime minister is the most politically powerful person in the country. The members of the government are chosen by the Prime Minister and there are ministers for each branch of the society. There are ministers for economy, finance, information technology, society, internal affairs, foreign affairs and other areas. The members of the Government are elected for a mandate of four years. Judiciary power is exercised by courts, with the court system being headed by the Judicial <a href="/wiki/Supreme_court" title="Supreme court">Supreme court</a>, Constitutional Court and the Republican Judicial Council. The assembly appoints the judges. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_North_Macedonia" title="Human rights in North Macedonia">Human rights in North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>North Macedonia is a signatory to the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a> and the UN Geneva <a href="/wiki/Convention_Relating_to_the_Status_of_Refugees" title="Convention Relating to the Status of Refugees">Convention Relating to the Status of Refugees</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Convention_Against_Torture" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Convention Against Torture">Convention against Torture</a>, and the Constitution guarantees basic human rights to all Macedonian citizens. </p>
      <p>According to human rights organisations, in 2003 there were suspected extrajudicial executions, threats against, and intimidation of, human rights activists and opposition journalists, and allegations of torture by the police.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hrw2006_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw2006-173">[166]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_North_Macedonia" title="Foreign relations of North Macedonia">Foreign relations of North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_North_Macedonia" title="List of diplomatic missions of North Macedonia">List of diplomatic missions of North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>North Macedonia became a member state of the UN on 8 April 1993, eighteen months after its independence from Yugoslavia. It was referred to within the UN as "the former Yugoslav Republic of Macedonia", until the resolution of the <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_naming_dispute" title="Macedonia naming dispute">long-running dispute</a> with Greece about the country's name. </p>
      <p>The major interest of the country is a full integration in the European and the <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/transatlantic" class="extiw" title="wikt:transatlantic">Trans-Atlantic</a> integration processes.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[167]</a></sup> Five foreign policy priorities are:<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[168]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Commencing negotiations for full-fledged membership in the European Union</li> 
       <li>Lifting the visa regime for Macedonian nationals</li> 
       <li>NATO membership</li> 
       <li>Resolving the naming issue with Greece</li> 
       <li>Strengthening the economic and public diplomacy</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>North Macedonia is a member of the following international and regional organisations:<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[169]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/IMF" class="mw-redirect" title="IMF">IMF</a> (since 1992), <a href="/wiki/WHO" class="mw-redirect" title="WHO">WHO</a> (since 1993), <a href="/wiki/EBRD" class="mw-redirect" title="EBRD">EBRD</a> (since 1993), <a href="/wiki/Central_European_Initiative" title="Central European Initiative">Central European Initiative</a> (since 1993), <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> (since 1995), <a href="/wiki/OSCE" class="mw-redirect" title="OSCE">OSCE</a> (since 1995), <a href="/wiki/Southeast_European_Cooperative_Initiative" title="Southeast European Cooperative Initiative">SECI</a> (since 1996), <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">La Francophonie</a> (since 2001), <a href="/wiki/WTO" class="mw-redirect" title="WTO">WTO</a> (since 2003), <a href="/wiki/CEFTA" class="mw-redirect" title="CEFTA">CEFTA</a> (since 2006), <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> (since 2020). </p>
      <p>In 2005, the country was officially recognised as a <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> candidate state. </p>
      <p>At the NATO <a href="/wiki/2008_Bucharest_summit" title="2008 Bucharest summit">2008 Bucharest summit</a>, Macedonia failed to gain an invitation to join the organisation because Greece vetoed the move after the dispute over the name issue.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[170]</a></sup> The U.S. had previously expressed support for an invitation,<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[171]</a></sup> but the summit then decided to extend an invitation only on condition of a resolution of the naming conflict with Greece. </p>
      <p>In March 2009, the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> expressed support for North Macedonia's EU candidacy and asked the EU Commission to grant the country a date for the start of accession talks by the end of 2009. The parliament also recommended a speedy lifting of the visa regime for Macedonian citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[172]</a></sup> Prior to the Prespa agreement, the country failed to receive a start date for accession talks as a result of the naming dispute. However, after the Prespa agreement, North Macedonia became a member state of NATO on 27 March 2020. The EU's stance was similar to NATO's in that resolution of the naming dispute was a precondition for the start of accession talks. </p>
      <p>In October 2012, the EU Enlargement Commissioner <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0tefan_F%C3%BCle" title="Å tefan FÃ¼le">Å tefan FÃ¼le</a> proposed a start of accession negotiations with the country for the fourth time, while the previous efforts were blocked each time by Greece. At the same time FÃ¼le visited Bulgaria in a bid to clarify the state's position with respect to Macedonia. He established that Bulgaria almost has joined Greece in vetoing the accession talks. The Bulgarian position was that Sofia cannot grant an EU certificate to Skopje, which is systematically employing an ideology of hate towards Bulgaria.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[173]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Republic_of_North_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Army of the Republic of North Macedonia">Army of the Republic of North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Macedonian_Soldiers_in_Kabul.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Macedonian_Soldiers_in_Kabul.jpg/220px-Macedonian_Soldiers_in_Kabul.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Macedonian_Soldiers_in_Kabul.jpg/330px-Macedonian_Soldiers_in_Kabul.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Macedonian_Soldiers_in_Kabul.jpg/440px-Macedonian_Soldiers_in_Kabul.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Macedonian_Soldiers_in_Kabul.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Republic_of_North_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Army of the Republic of North Macedonia">Army of the Republic of North Macedonia</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Army_of_North_Macedonia" title="Army of North Macedonia">military of North Macedonia</a> comprises the army, <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Air_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedonian Air Force">air force</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wolves_(military)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wolves (military)">special forces</a>. The government's national defence policy aims to guarantee the preservation of the independence and sovereignty of the state, the integrity of its land area and airspace and its constitutional order. Its main goals remain the development and maintenance of a credible capability to defend the nation's vital interests and development of the Armed Forces in a way that ensures their interoperability with the armed forces of NATO and the European Union member states and their capability to participate in the full range of NATO missions. </p>
      <p>The Ministry of Defence develops the Republic's defence strategy and assesses possible threats and risks. It is also responsible for the defence system, including training, readiness, equipment, and development, and for drawing up and presenting the defence budget.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[174]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Naming_dispute">Naming dispute</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_naming_dispute" title="Macedonia naming dispute">Macedonia naming dispute</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(terminology)" title="Macedonia (terminology)">Macedonia (terminology)</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Macedonia_(1992%E2%80%931995).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Flag_of_Macedonia_%281992%E2%80%931995%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Macedonia_%281992%E2%80%931995%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Flag_of_Macedonia_%281992%E2%80%931995%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Macedonia_%281992%E2%80%931995%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Flag_of_Macedonia_%281992%E2%80%931995%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Macedonia_%281992%E2%80%931995%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="300"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Macedonia_(1992%E2%80%931995).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The flag of the then-Republic of Macedonia between 1992 and 1995, bearing the <a href="/wiki/Vergina_Sun" title="Vergina Sun">Vergina Sun</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The use of the name <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(terminology)" title="Macedonia (terminology)">"Macedonia"</a> was disputed between Greece and North Macedonia. The specific naming dispute was reignited after the <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia" title="Breakup of Yugoslavia">breakup of Yugoslavia</a> and the newly gained independence of the former Socialist Republic of Macedonia in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[175]</a></sup> Greece opposed the use of the name without a geographical qualifier so as to avoid confusion with its own region of <a href="/wiki/Greek_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Macedonia">Greek Macedonia</a> to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[176]</a></sup> As some ethnic Greeks identify themselves as Macedonians, unrelated to the Slavic people who are associated with North Macedonia, Greece further objected to the use of the term <i>Macedonian</i> for the neighbouring country's largest ethnic group; it accused the country of appropriating symbols and figures that are historically considered parts of <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Greece" title="Culture of Greece">Greece's culture</a> (such as <a href="/wiki/Vergina_Sun" title="Vergina Sun">Vergina Sun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a>), and of promoting the <a href="/wiki/Irredentist" class="mw-redirect" title="Irredentist">irredentist</a> concept of a <a href="/wiki/United_Macedonia" title="United Macedonia">United Macedonia</a>, which would include territories of Greece, Bulgaria, Albania, and Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[177]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UN adopted the provisional reference <i>the former Yugoslav Republic of Macedonia</i> (<a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">ÐÐ¾ÑÐ°Ð½ÐµÑÐ½Ð° ÐÑÐ³Ð¾ÑÐ»Ð¾Ð²ÐµÐ½ÑÐºÐ° Ð ÐµÐ¿ÑÐ±Ð»Ð¸ÐºÐ° ÐÐ°ÐºÐµÐ´Ð¾Ð½Ð¸ÑÐ°</span>) when the country was admitted to the organisation in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN-185">[178]</a></sup> The lower-cased "former" was chosen intentionally to display the provisionality of the name although most UN member countries soon abandoned the provisional reference and recognised the country as the <i>Republic of Macedonia</i> instead.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[179]</a></sup> Most international organisations adopted the same convention along with over 100 UN members and four of the five permanent <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">UN Security Council</a> members.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[181]</a></sup> In the period between 1991 and 2019, the country's name was an ongoing issue in bilateral and international relations. The UN set up a negotiating process with a mediator, <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Nimetz" title="Matthew Nimetz">Matthew Nimetz</a>, and the two parties to try to mediate the dispute. Following the ratification of the Prespa agreement, most major international organisations welcomed the settlement of the long-standing dispute, and adopted the country's new name.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[182]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[184]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">Subdivisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Statistical_regions_of_North_Macedonia" title="Statistical regions of North Macedonia">Statistical regions of North Macedonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_North_Macedonia" title="Municipalities of North Macedonia">Municipalities of North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_urban_and_rural_municipalities_of_North_Macedonia_en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Map_of_urban_and_rural_municipalities_of_North_Macedonia_en.svg/220px-Map_of_urban_and_rural_municipalities_of_North_Macedonia_en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Map_of_urban_and_rural_municipalities_of_North_Macedonia_en.svg/330px-Map_of_urban_and_rural_municipalities_of_North_Macedonia_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Map_of_urban_and_rural_municipalities_of_North_Macedonia_en.svg/440px-Map_of_urban_and_rural_municipalities_of_North_Macedonia_en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="744" data-file-height="581"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_urban_and_rural_municipalities_of_North_Macedonia_en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Rural/Urban municipalities
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MSR.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/MSR.png/220px-MSR.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/MSR.png/330px-MSR.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/MSR.png/440px-MSR.png 2x" data-file-width="528" data-file-height="431"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MSR.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Statistical regions of North Macedonia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>North Macedonia's statistical regions exist solely for legal and statistical purposes. The regions are: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Eastern_statistical_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern statistical region">Eastern</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Northeastern_statistical_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Northeastern statistical region">Northeastern</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Pelagonia_statistical_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Pelagonia statistical region">Pelagonia</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Polog_statistical_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Polog statistical region">Polog</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Skopje_statistical_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Skopje statistical region">Skopje</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Southeastern_statistical_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern statistical region">Southeastern</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Southwestern_statistical_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Southwestern statistical region">Southwestern</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Vardar_statistical_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Vardar statistical region">Vardar</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>In August 2004, the country was reorganised into 84 municipalities (<i lang="mk" title="Macedonian-language text">opÅ¡tini</i>; sing. <i lang="mk" title="Macedonian-language text">opÅ¡tina</i>); 10 of the municipalities constitute the City of <a href="/wiki/Skopje" title="Skopje">Skopje</a>, a distinct unit of local self-government and the country's capital. </p>
      <p>Most of the current municipalities were unaltered or merely amalgamated from the previous 123 municipalities established in September 1996; others were consolidated and their borders changed. Prior to this, local government was organised into 34 administrative districts, communes, or counties (also opÅ¡tini). </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_North_Macedonia" title="Economy of North Macedonia">Economy of North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Ranked as the fourth "best reformatory state" out of 178 countries ranked by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> in 2009, North Macedonia has undergone considerable economic reform since independence.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-192">[185]</a></sup> The country has developed an <a href="/wiki/Open_economy" title="Open economy">open economy</a> with trade accounting for more than 90% of GDP in recent years. Since 1996, North Macedonia has witnessed steady, though slow, economic growth with GDP growing by 3.1% in 2005. This figure was projected to rise to an average of 5.2% in the 2006â2010 period.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank-devdata_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-devdata-193">[186]</a></sup> The government has proven successful in its efforts to combat inflation, with an <a href="/wiki/Inflation_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Inflation rate">inflation rate</a> of only 3% in 2006 and 2% in 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank_192-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-192">[185]</a></sup> and has implemented policies focused on attracting <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign investment</a> and promoting the development of small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs). </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%93%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%98%D0%B5_-_%D0%92%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/%D0%93%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%98%D0%B5_-_%D0%92%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86.jpg/220px-%D0%93%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%98%D0%B5_-_%D0%92%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/%D0%93%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%98%D0%B5_-_%D0%92%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86.jpg/330px-%D0%93%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%98%D0%B5_-_%D0%92%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/%D0%93%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%98%D0%B5_-_%D0%92%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86.jpg/440px-%D0%93%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%98%D0%B5_-_%D0%92%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%93%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%98%D0%B5_-_%D0%92%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Vineyard in North Macedonia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The current government introduced a <a href="/wiki/Flat_tax" title="Flat tax">flat tax</a> system with the intention of making the country more attractive to foreign investment. The flat tax rate was 12% in 2007 and was further lowered to 10% in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[188]</a></sup> Despite these reforms, as of 2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=North_Macedonia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> North Macedonia's <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment rate</a> was 37.2%<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[189]</a></sup> and as of 2006<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=North_Macedonia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> its <a href="/wiki/Poverty_threshold" title="Poverty threshold">poverty rate</a> was 22%.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank-devdata_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-devdata-193">[186]</a></sup> Due to a number of employment measures as well as the successful process of attracting multinational corporations, and according to the State Statistical Office of North Macedonia, the country's unemployment rate in the first quarter of 2015 decreased to 27.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[190]</a></sup> Government's policies and efforts in regards to foreign direct investments have resulted with the establishment of local subsidiaries of several world leading manufacturing companies, especially from the automotive industry, such as: <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Controls" title="Johnson Controls">Johnson Controls Inc.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Van_Hool" title="Van Hool">Van Hool NV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Matthey" title="Johnson Matthey">Johnson Matthey plc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lear_Corporation" title="Lear Corporation">Lear Corp.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visteon" title="Visteon">Visteon Corp.</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kostal-Gruppe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kostal-Gruppe (page does not exist)">Kostal GmbH</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gentherm_Incorporated" title="Gentherm Incorporated">Gentherm Inc.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dr%C3%A4xlmaier_Group" title="DrÃ¤xlmaier Group">DrÃ¤xlmaier Group</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kromberg_%26_Schubert&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kromberg &amp; Schubert (page does not exist)">Kromberg &amp; Schubert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marquardt_Group" title="Marquardt Group">Marquardt GmbH</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amphenol" title="Amphenol">Amphenol Corp.</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tekno_Hose_SpA&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tekno Hose SpA (page does not exist)">Tekno Hose SpA</a>, <a href="/wiki/KEMET_Corporation" title="KEMET Corporation">KEMET Corp.</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_Safety_Systems_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Key Safety Systems Inc. (page does not exist)">Key Safety Systems Inc.</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=ODW-Elektrik_GmbH&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ODW-Elektrik GmbH (page does not exist)">ODW-Elektrik GmbH</a>, etc. </p>
      <p>In terms of GDP structure, as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=North_Macedonia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the manufacturing sector, including mining and construction constituted the largest part of GDP at 21.4%, up from 21.1% in 2012. The trade, transportation and accommodation sector represents 18.2% of GDP in 2013, up from 16.7% in 2012, while agriculture represents 9.6%, up from 9.1% in the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[191]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Macedonia_treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Macedonia_treemap.png/220px-Macedonia_treemap.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Macedonia_treemap.png/330px-Macedonia_treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Macedonia_treemap.png/440px-Macedonia_treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="1105" data-file-height="865"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Macedonia_treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of North Macedonia's product exports.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In terms of foreign trade, the largest sector contributing to the country's export in 2014 was "chemicals and related products" at 21.4%, followed by the "machinery and transport equipment" sector at 21.1%. North Macedonia's main import sectors in 2014 were "manufactured goods classified chiefly by material" with 34.2%, "machinery and transport equipment" with 18.7% and "mineral fuels, lubricants and related materials" with 14.4% of the total imports. Even 68.8% of the foreign trade in 2014 was done with the EU which makes the Union by far the largest trading partner of North Macedonia (23.3% with Germany, 7.9% with the UK, 7.3% with Greece, 6.2% with Italy, etc.). Almost 12% of the total external trade in 2014 was done with the Western Balkan countries.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[192]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>North Macedonia has one of the highest shares of people struggling financially, with 72% of its citizens stating that they could manage on their household's income only "with difficulty" or "with great difficulty", though North Macedonia, along with Croatia, was the only country in the Western Balkans to not report an increase in this statistic.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[193]</a></sup> Corruption and a relatively ineffective legal system also act as significant restraints on successful <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">economic development</a>. North Macedonia still has one of the lowest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">per capita GDPs</a> in Europe. Furthermore, the country's <a href="/wiki/Grey_market" title="Grey market">grey market</a> is estimated at close to 20% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[194]</a></sup> PPS GDP per capita stood at 36% of the EU average in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[195]</a></sup> With a GDP per capita of US$9,157 at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> and a <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> of 0.701, North Macedonia is less developed and has a considerably smaller economy than most of the former Yugoslav states. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade">Trade</span></h3> 
      <p>The outbreak of the Yugoslav wars and the imposition of sanctions on <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Serbia and Montenegro</a> caused great damage to the country's economy, with Serbia constituting 60% of its markets before the disintegration of Yugoslavia. When Greece imposed a <a href="/wiki/Trade_embargo" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade embargo">trade embargo</a> on the Republic in 1994â95, the economy was also affected. Some relief was afforded by the end of the <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnian War</a> in November 1995 and the lifting of the Greek embargo, but the Kosovo War of 1999 and the 2001 Albanian crisis caused further destabilisation. </p>
      <p>Since the end of the Greek embargo, Greece has become the country's most important business partner. (See <a href="/wiki/Greek_investments_in_North_Macedonia" title="Greek investments in North Macedonia">Greek investments in North Macedonia</a>.) Many Greek companies have bought former state companies in North Macedonia,<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[196]</a></sup> such as the <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">oil refinery</a> Okta, the baking company Zhito Luks, a marble mine in <a href="/wiki/Prilep" title="Prilep">Prilep</a>, textile facilities in Bitola, etc., and employ 20,000 people. The moving of business to North Macedonia in the oil sector has been caused by the rise of Greece in the oil markets.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[197]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other key partners are Germany, Italy, the United States, Slovenia, Austria and Turkey. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_North_Macedonia" title="Tourism in North Macedonia">Tourism in North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ohrid_Lake.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Ohrid_Lake.jpg/220px-Ohrid_Lake.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Ohrid_Lake.jpg/330px-Ohrid_Lake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Ohrid_Lake.jpg/440px-Ohrid_Lake.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1540"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ohrid_Lake.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._John_at_Kaneo" title="Church of St. John at Kaneo">church of St. John at Kaneo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ohrid" title="Lake Ohrid">Lake Ohrid</a>, one of the most popular tourist destinations in North Macedonia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">Tourism</a> plays a significant role in the economy of North Macedonia accounting for 6.7% of its GDP in 2016. The annual income from tourism was estimated at 38.5 billion denars (â¬616 million) in that year.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[198]</a></sup> Following its independence, the most serious negative impact on tourism performance occurred due to the armed conflicts taking place in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-marinoski_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marinoski-206">[199]</a></sup> The number of foreign visitors has been on the rise since, with a 14.6% increase in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-207">[200]</a></sup> In 2019, North Macedonia received 1,184,963 tourist arrivals out of which 757,593 foreign.<sup id="cite_ref-State_Statistical_Office_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_Statistical_Office-208">[201]</a></sup> Most numerous are tourists from <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, neighboring Serbia, Greece and Bulgaria, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> and other countries of Western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-tourism2019_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism2019-209">[202]</a></sup> The biggest bulk of tourists, approximately 60% of the million tourists that visited the country in 2017, was situated in Skopje and the southwestern region of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[203]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The most significant tourism branches are lake tourism as there are three lakes in Ohrid, Prespa and Dojran and over 50 small glacial lakes of variable sizes, mountainous tourism as there are 16 mountains higher than 2,000 metres. Other forms of tourism also include rural and ecotourism, city tourism and <a href="/wiki/Cultural_tourism" title="Cultural tourism">cultural tourism</a>, represented through gastronomy, traditional music, cultural celebrations and cultural heritage sites.<sup id="cite_ref-marinoski_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marinoski-206">[199]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_North_Macedonia" title="Transport in North Macedonia">Transport in North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:North_Macedonian_Highway_System.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/North_Macedonian_Highway_System.svg/220px-North_Macedonian_Highway_System.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/North_Macedonian_Highway_System.svg/330px-North_Macedonian_Highway_System.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/North_Macedonian_Highway_System.svg/440px-North_Macedonian_Highway_System.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="424"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:North_Macedonian_Highway_System.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of current and planned highways
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>North Macedonia (along with <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and Kosovo) belongs to the less-developed southern region of the former Yugoslavia. It suffered severe economic difficulties after independence, when the Yugoslav <a href="/wiki/Internal_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal market">internal market</a> collapsed and subsidies from Belgrade ended. In addition, it faced many of the same problems faced by other former socialist <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">East European</a> countries during the transition to a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>. Its main land and rail exports route, through Serbia, remains unreliable with high transit costs, thereby affecting the export of its formerly highly profitable, early vegetables market to Germany. </p>
      <p>North Macedonia's IT market increased 63.8% year on year in 2007, which was the fastest growing in the Adriatic region.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[204]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>North Macedonia is in its position a continental country in the middle of the Balkan peninsula, and the main transport links in the country are those that connect the different parts of the peninsula (transbalkan links). Particularly important is the connection between northâsouth and Vardar valley, which connects Greece with the rest of Europe. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D0%B2%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%81_-_%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_-_%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/%D0%90%D0%B2%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%81_-_%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_-_%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG/220px-%D0%90%D0%B2%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%81_-_%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_-_%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/%D0%90%D0%B2%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%81_-_%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_-_%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG/330px-%D0%90%D0%B2%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%81_-_%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_-_%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/%D0%90%D0%B2%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%81_-_%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_-_%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG/440px-%D0%90%D0%B2%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%81_-_%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_-_%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D0%B2%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%81_-_%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_-_%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/European_route_E75" title="European route E75">European route E75</a> in North Macedonia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The total length of the railway network in North Macedonia is 699&nbsp;km (434&nbsp;mi). Operated by <a href="/wiki/Makedonski_%C5%BDeleznici" title="Makedonski Å½eleznici">Makedonski Å½eleznici</a>, the most important railway line is the line on the border with SerbiaâKumanovoâSkopjeâVelesâGevgelijaâborder with Greece. Since 2001, the railway line Beljakovci has been builtâthe border with Bulgaria, which will get a direct connection Skopje-Sofia. The most important railway hub in the country is Skopje, while the other two are Veles and Kumanovo. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="North Macedonia Post">North Macedonia Post</a> is the state-owned company for the provision of postal traffic. It was founded in 1992 as PTT Macedonia. In 1993 it was admitted to the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Postal_Union" title="Universal Postal Union">World Postal Union</a> in 1997, PTT Macedonia was divided into Macedonian Telekom and Macedonian Post (later renamed North Macedonia Post). </p>
      <p>As far as water transport is concerned, only lake traffic through Ohrid and Prespan Lake has been developed, mostly for tourist purposes. </p>
      <p>There are 17 airports officially in North Macedonia, of which 11 are with solid substrates. Among them are two airports of international character, since they are listed on the airport's <a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA airport code</a> <a href="/wiki/International_Airport_Skopje" class="mw-redirect" title="International Airport Skopje">International Airport Skopje</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ohrid_St._Paul_the_Apostle_Airport" title="Ohrid St. Paul the Apostle Airport">Ohrid St. Paul the Apostle Airport</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ss_Cyril_and_Methodius_University_campus_Skopje.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Ss_Cyril_and_Methodius_University_campus_Skopje.jpg/220px-Ss_Cyril_and_Methodius_University_campus_Skopje.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Ss_Cyril_and_Methodius_University_campus_Skopje.jpg/330px-Ss_Cyril_and_Methodius_University_campus_Skopje.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Ss_Cyril_and_Methodius_University_campus_Skopje.jpg/440px-Ss_Cyril_and_Methodius_University_campus_Skopje.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ss_Cyril_and_Methodius_University_campus_Skopje.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Ss._Cyril_and_Methodius_University_of_Skopje" title="Ss. Cyril and Methodius University of Skopje">Ss. Cyril and Methodius University</a> in Skopje.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The higher levels of <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a> can be obtained at one of the five state universities: <a href="/wiki/Ss._Cyril_and_Methodius_University_of_Skopje" title="Ss. Cyril and Methodius University of Skopje">Ss. Cyril and Methodius University of Skopje</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Clement_of_Ohrid_University_of_Bitola" title="St. Clement of Ohrid University of Bitola">St. Clement of Ohrid University of Bitola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goce_Del%C4%8Dev_University_of_%C5%A0tip" title="Goce DelÄev University of Å tip">Goce DelÄev University of Å tip</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_Tetova" title="State University of Tetova">State University of Tetova</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Information_Science_and_Technology_%22St._Paul_The_Apostle%22" title="University of Information Science and Technology &quot;St. Paul The Apostle&quot;">University of Information Science and Technology "St. Paul The Apostle"</a> in Ohrid. There are a number of private university institutions, such as the European University,<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[205]</a></sup> Slavic University in <a href="/wiki/Sveti_Nikole" title="Sveti Nikole">Sveti Nikole</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_East_European_University" title="South East European University">South East European University</a> and others. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Agency_for_International_Development" title="United States Agency for International Development">United States Agency for International Development</a> has underwritten a project called <i>Macedonia Connects</i>, which has made North Macedonia the first all-broadband wireless country in the world. The Ministry of Education and Sciences reports that 461 schools (primary and secondary) are now connected to the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[206]</a></sup> In addition, an <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">Internet service provider</a> (On.net), has created a MESH Network to provide WIFI services in the 11 largest cities/towns in the country. The national library of North Macedonia, <a href="/wiki/National_and_University_Library_%22St._Kliment_of_Ohrid%22" title="National and University Library &quot;St. Kliment of Ohrid&quot;">National and University Library "St. Kliment of Ohrid"</a>, is in Skopje. </p>
      <p>The North Macedonian education system consists of: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">pre-school education</a></li> 
       <li>primary</li> 
       <li>secondary</li> 
       <li>higher</li>
      </ul> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div>

      <p>The last census data from 2002 shows a population of 2,022,547 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-stat.gov.mk_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat.gov.mk-4">[2]</a></sup> The last official estimate from 2009, without significant change, gives a figure of 2,050,671.<sup id="cite_ref-dzs_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dzs-214">[207]</a></sup> According to the last census data, the largest ethnic group in the country are the ethnic <a href="/wiki/Macedonians_(ethnic_group)" title="Macedonians (ethnic group)">Macedonians</a>. The second-largest group are the <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_North_Macedonia" title="Albanians in North Macedonia">Albanians</a>, who dominated much of the northwestern part of the country. Following them, <a href="/wiki/Turks_in_North_Macedonia" title="Turks in North Macedonia">Turks</a> are the third-biggest ethnic group of the country where official census data put them close to 80,000 and unofficial estimates suggest numbers between 170,000 and 200,000. Some unofficial estimates indicate that there are possibly up to 260,000 <a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_North_Macedonia" title="Romani people in North Macedonia">Romani</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[208]</a></sup> </p>

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_North_Macedonia" title="Religion in North Macedonia">Religion in North Macedonia</a>

        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p>Religion in North Macedonia (2011)<sup id="cite_ref-2011data_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011data-5">[3]</a></sup> </p> 
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Red; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodoxy</a> (69.6%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">

         </div>

         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:DeepSkyBlue; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Other <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> (0.7%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:MediumSeaGreen; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (28.6%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Honeydew; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;None (0.5%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Chartreuse; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Others (0.2%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Christianity</a> is the majority faith of North Macedonia, making up 65% of the population, the vast majority of whom belong to the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Orthodox_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedonian Orthodox Church">Macedonian Orthodox Church</a>. Various other Christian denominations account for 0.4% of the population. Muslims constitute 33.3% of the population. North Macedonia has the fifth-highest proportion of Muslims in Europe, after those of Kosovo (96%),<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[209]</a></sup> Turkey (90%),<sup id="cite_ref-onedio.com_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-onedio.com-217">[210]</a></sup> Albania (59%),<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[211]</a></sup> and Bosnia and Herzegovina (51%).<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[212]</a></sup> Most Muslims are Albanians, Turks, or Romani; few are <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Muslims" title="Macedonian Muslims">Macedonian Muslims</a>. The remaining 1.4% was determined to be "unaffiliated" by a 2010 Pew Research estimation.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew1_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew1-220">[213]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>All together, there were 1,842 churches and 580 mosques in the country at the end of 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-dnevnik_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dnevnik-221">[214]</a></sup> The Orthodox and Islamic religious communities have secondary religion schools in Skopje. There is an Orthodox <a href="/wiki/Seminary" title="Seminary">theological college</a> in the capital. The Macedonian Orthodox Church has jurisdiction over 10 provinces (seven in the country and three abroad), has 10 bishops and about 350 priests. A total of 30,000 people are baptised in all the provinces every year. </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:308px;max-width:308px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%A1%D0%B2_%D0%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%92%D0%B0.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%A1%D0%B2_%D0%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%92%D0%B0.JPG/150px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%A1%D0%B2_%D0%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%92%D0%B0.JPG" decoding="async" width="150" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%A1%D0%B2_%D0%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%92%D0%B0.JPG/225px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%A1%D0%B2_%D0%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%92%D0%B0.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%A1%D0%B2_%D0%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%92%D0%B0.JPG/300px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%A1%D0%B2_%D0%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%92%D0%B0.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3648"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Kalkandelen_-_Alaca_Cami_R01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Kalkandelen_-_Alaca_Cami_R01.JPG/150px-Kalkandelen_-_Alaca_Cami_R01.JPG" decoding="async" width="150" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Kalkandelen_-_Alaca_Cami_R01.JPG/225px-Kalkandelen_-_Alaca_Cami_R01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Kalkandelen_-_Alaca_Cami_R01.JPG/300px-Kalkandelen_-_Alaca_Cami_R01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3800" data-file-height="5067"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._George,_Staro_Nagori%C4%8Dane" title="Church of St. George, Staro NagoriÄane">The Church of St. George</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kumanovo" title="Kumanovo">Kumanovo</a> (left) and <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0arena_D%C5%BEamija" class="mw-redirect" title="Å arena DÅ¾amija">Å arena DÅ¾amija Mosque</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tetovo" title="Tetovo">Tetovo</a> (right)
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Relations between the Macedonian Orthodox Church, which declared <a href="/wiki/Autocephaly" title="Autocephaly">autocephaly</a> in 1967 and remains unrecognised by the other Orthodox Churches, and the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox Church</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Ohrid_Archbishopric" title="Orthodox Ohrid Archbishopric">claims ecclesiastical jurisdiction</a> over North Macedonia, remain tense and politically fraught, especially since the Serbian Church appointed <a href="/wiki/Jovan_Vrani%C5%A1kovski" title="Jovan VraniÅ¡kovski">Jovan VraniÅ¡kovski</a> as its Exarch for the Archbishopric of Ohrid in September 2002. </p>
      <p>The reaction of the Macedonian Orthodox Church was to cut off all relations with the new Ohrid Archbishopric and to prevent bishops of the Serbian Orthodox Church from entering North Macedonia. Bishop Jovan was jailed for 18&nbsp;months for "defaming the Macedonian Orthodox church and harming the religious feelings of local citizens" by distributing Serbian Orthodox church calendars and pamphlets.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[215]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0_-_%D7%9E%D7%A7%D7%93%D7%95%D7%A0%D7%99_%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%95%D7%9B%D7%99%D7%99%D7%94_-_Macedonian_Hanukkah_menorah.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0_-_%D7%9E%D7%A7%D7%93%D7%95%D7%A0%D7%99_%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%95%D7%9B%D7%99%D7%99%D7%94_-_Macedonian_Hanukkah_menorah.jpg/220px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0_-_%D7%9E%D7%A7%D7%93%D7%95%D7%A0%D7%99_%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%95%D7%9B%D7%99%D7%99%D7%94_-_Macedonian_Hanukkah_menorah.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0_-_%D7%9E%D7%A7%D7%93%D7%95%D7%A0%D7%99_%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%95%D7%9B%D7%99%D7%99%D7%94_-_Macedonian_Hanukkah_menorah.jpg/330px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0_-_%D7%9E%D7%A7%D7%93%D7%95%D7%A0%D7%99_%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%95%D7%9B%D7%99%D7%99%D7%94_-_Macedonian_Hanukkah_menorah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0_-_%D7%9E%D7%A7%D7%93%D7%95%D7%A0%D7%99_%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%95%D7%9B%D7%99%D7%99%D7%94_-_Macedonian_Hanukkah_menorah.jpg/440px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0_-_%D7%9E%D7%A7%D7%93%D7%95%D7%A0%D7%99_%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%95%D7%9B%D7%99%D7%99%D7%94_-_Macedonian_Hanukkah_menorah.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3400" data-file-height="2432"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0_-_%D7%9E%D7%A7%D7%93%D7%95%D7%A0%D7%99_%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%95%D7%9B%D7%99%D7%99%D7%94_-_Macedonian_Hanukkah_menorah.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A 19th-century silver <a href="/wiki/Menorah_(Hanukkah)" title="Menorah (Hanukkah)">Hanukkah Menorah</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Greek_Catholic_Church" title="Macedonian Greek Catholic Church">Macedonian Byzantine Catholic Church</a> has approximately 11,000 adherents in North Macedonia. The Church was established in 1918, and is made up mostly of converts to Catholicism and their descendants. The Church is of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Rite" title="Byzantine Rite">Byzantine Rite</a> and is in communion with the Roman and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic_Churches" title="Eastern Catholic Churches">Eastern Catholic Churches</a>. Its liturgical worship is performed in Macedonian.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[216]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There is a small <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> community. The most famous Protestant in the country is the late president <a href="/wiki/Boris_Trajkovski" title="Boris Trajkovski">Boris Trajkovski</a>. He was from the <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodist</a> community, which is the largest and oldest Protestant church in the Republic, dating back to the late 19th century. Since the 1980s the Protestant community has grown, partly through new confidence and partly with outside missionary help. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_North_Macedonia" title="History of the Jews in North Macedonia">Macedonian Jewish community</a>, which numbered some 7,200 people on the eve of World War II, was almost entirely destroyed during the war: only 2% survived <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[217]</a></sup> After their liberation and the end of the War, most opted to emigrate to <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. Today, the country's Jewish community numbers approximately 200 persons, almost all of whom live in Skopje. Most Macedonian Jews are <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardic</a>âthe descendants of 15th-century refugees who had been expelled from <a href="/wiki/Alhambra_Decree" title="Alhambra Decree">Castile, Aragon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Jews_and_Muslims_by_Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Persecution of Jews and Muslims by Manuel I of Portugal">Portugal</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_North_Macedonia" title="Languages of North Macedonia">Languages of North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Political_views_on_the_Macedonian_language" title="Political views on the Macedonian language">Political views on the Macedonian language</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Makedonija_-_Jezicki_sastav_po_naseljima_2002.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Makedonija_-_Jezicki_sastav_po_naseljima_2002.gif/220px-Makedonija_-_Jezicki_sastav_po_naseljima_2002.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Makedonija_-_Jezicki_sastav_po_naseljima_2002.gif/330px-Makedonija_-_Jezicki_sastav_po_naseljima_2002.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Makedonija_-_Jezicki_sastav_po_naseljima_2002.gif/440px-Makedonija_-_Jezicki_sastav_po_naseljima_2002.gif 2x" data-file-width="3700" data-file-height="3283"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Makedonija_-_Jezicki_sastav_po_naseljima_2002.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Linguistic map of North Macedonia, 2002 census
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>National and official language in all aspects of the whole territory of North Macedonia and in its international relations, is the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian language</a>. <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a> is co-official at a state level (excluding defence, central police and monetary policy) and in local self-government units where speakers are 20% or more. Macedonian belongs to the Eastern branch of the <a href="/wiki/South_Slavic_languages" title="South Slavic languages">South Slavic language group</a>, while Albanian occupies an independent branch of the <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European family of languages</a>. In municipalities where at least 20% of the population is part of another ethnic minority, those individual languages are used for official purposes in local government, alongside Macedonian and Albanian or just Macedonian. </p>
      <p>Macedonian is closely related to and <a href="/wiki/Mutual_intelligibility" title="Mutual intelligibility">mutually intelligible</a> with standard <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>. It also has some similarities with standard <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a> and the intermediate <a href="/wiki/Torlakian_dialect" title="Torlakian dialect">Torlakian</a>/<a href="/wiki/Shopi#Dialects" title="Shopi">Shop</a> dialects spoken mostly in southeastern Serbia and western Bulgaria (and by speakers in the northeast of Macedonia). The <a href="/wiki/Standard_language" title="Standard language">standard language</a> was <a href="/wiki/Codification_(linguistics)" title="Codification (linguistics)">codified</a> in the period following World War II and has accumulated a thriving literary tradition. </p>
      <p>Besides Macedonian and Albanian, minority languages with substantial numbers of speakers are <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Gagauz_Turkish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Gagauz Turkish language">Balkan Gagauz</a><sup id="cite_ref-Ethnologue_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnologue-225">[218]</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>/<a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">Bosnian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aromanian_language" title="Aromanian language">Aromanian</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Megleno-Romanian_language" title="Megleno-Romanian language">Megleno-Romanian</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Eurominority_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurominority-226">[219]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-228">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-229">[222]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eupedia_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eupedia-230">[223]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Sign_Language" title="Macedonian Sign Language">Macedonian Sign Language</a> is the primary language of those of the deaf community who did not pick up an oral language in childhood. </p>
      <p>According to the last census, 1,344,815 citizens of North Macedonia declared that they spoke Macedonian, 507,989 declared Albanian, 71,757 Turkish, 38,528 Romani, 24,773 Serbian, 8,560 Bosnian, 6,884 Aromanian and 19,241 spoke other languages.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-3">[1]</a></sup> </p>
