      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_North_Macedonia" title="Culture of North Macedonia">Culture of North Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Macedonians_(ethnic_group)" title="List of Macedonians (ethnic group)">List of Macedonians (ethnic group)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_North_Macedonia" title="Music of North Macedonia">Music of North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tanec_folk_ensemble_Macedonia_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tanec_folk_ensemble_Macedonia_3.jpg/220px-Tanec_folk_ensemble_Macedonia_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tanec_folk_ensemble_Macedonia_3.jpg/330px-Tanec_folk_ensemble_Macedonia_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tanec_folk_ensemble_Macedonia_3.jpg/440px-Tanec_folk_ensemble_Macedonia_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="845" data-file-height="634"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tanec_folk_ensemble_Macedonia_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Female folk dancers
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>North Macedonia has a rich cultural heritage in art, architecture, poetry and music. It has many ancient, protected religious sites. Poetry, cinema, and music festivals are held annually. <a href="/wiki/Music_of_North_Macedonia" title="Music of North Macedonia">Macedonian music</a> styles developed under the strong influence of <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_music" title="Byzantine music">Byzantine</a> church music. North Macedonia has a significant number of preserved <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_art" title="Byzantine art">Byzantine</a> <a href="/wiki/Fresco" title="Fresco">fresco</a> paintings, mainly from the period between the 11th and 16th centuries. There are several thousands of square metres of fresco painting preserved, the major part of which is in very good condition and represent masterworks of the Macedonian school of ecclesiastical painting. </p>
      <p>The most important cultural events in the country are the <a href="/wiki/Ohrid" title="Ohrid">Ohrid</a> Summer festival of classical music and drama, the <a href="/wiki/Struga_Poetry_Evenings" title="Struga Poetry Evenings">Struga Poetry Evenings</a> which gather poets from more than 50 countries in the world, International Camera Festival in <a href="/wiki/Bitola" title="Bitola">Bitola</a>, Open Youth Theatre and <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Jazz_Festival" title="Skopje Jazz Festival">Skopje Jazz Festival</a> in Skopje etc. The National Opera opened in 1947, then named "Macedonian Opera", with a performance of <i><a href="/wiki/Cavalleria_rusticana" title="Cavalleria rusticana">Cavalleria rusticana</a></i> under the direction of Branko Pomorisac. Every year, the May Opera Evenings are held in Skopje for around 20 nights. The first May Opera performance was that of <a href="/wiki/Kiril_Makedonski" title="Kiril Makedonski">Kiril Makedonski</a>'s <i>Tsar Samuil</i> in May 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[224]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_cuisine" title="Macedonian cuisine">Macedonian cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%93%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B0(%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%87%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%87%D0%B5)_(3).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/%D0%93%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B0%28%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%87%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%87%D0%B5%29_%283%29.jpg/220px-%D0%93%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B0%28%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%87%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%87%D0%B5%29_%283%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/%D0%93%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B0%28%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%87%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%87%D0%B5%29_%283%29.jpg/330px-%D0%93%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B0%28%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%87%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%87%D0%B5%29_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/%D0%93%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B0%28%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%87%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%87%D0%B5%29_%283%29.jpg/440px-%D0%93%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B0%28%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%87%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%87%D0%B5%29_%283%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5000" data-file-height="3337"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%93%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B0(%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%87%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%87%D0%B5)_(3).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Tav%C4%8De_grav%C4%8De" title="TavÄe gravÄe">TavÄe gravÄe</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The country's cuisine is a representative of that of the Balkansâreflecting <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_cuisine" title="Mediterranean cuisine">Mediterranean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_Eastern_cuisine" title="Middle Eastern cuisine">Middle Eastern</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ottoman_cuisine" title="Ottoman cuisine">Ottoman</a>) influences, and to a lesser extent <a href="/wiki/Italian_cuisine" title="Italian cuisine">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_cuisine" title="German cuisine">German</a> and Eastern European (especially <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_cuisine" title="Hungarian cuisine">Hungarian</a>) ones.<sup id="cite_ref-friedman_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-friedman-232">[225]</a></sup> The relatively warm climate in North Macedonia provides excellent growth conditions for a variety of vegetables, herbs and fruits. Thus, Macedonian cuisine is particularly diverse. </p>
      <p>Macedonian cuisine is also noted for the diversity and quality of its <a href="/wiki/Dairy_products" class="mw-redirect" title="Dairy products">dairy products</a>, wines, and local alcoholic beverages, such as <a href="/wiki/Rakija" class="mw-redirect" title="Rakija">rakija</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tav%C4%8De_grav%C4%8De" title="TavÄe gravÄe">TavÄe gravÄe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mastika" title="Mastika">mastika</a> are considered the national dish and drink of North Macedonia, respectively. Some other important dishes include <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0opska_salad" class="mw-redirect" title="Å opska salad">Å opska salad</a>, an appetiser and side dish that accompanies the main meal, <a href="/wiki/Ajvar" title="Ajvar">ajvar</a>, stuffed peppers, <a href="/wiki/Pastrmajlija" title="Pastrmajlija">pastrmajlija</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[226]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SStandPhilipIIArena.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/SStandPhilipIIArena.jpg/220px-SStandPhilipIIArena.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="98" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/SStandPhilipIIArena.jpg/330px-SStandPhilipIIArena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/SStandPhilipIIArena.jpg/440px-SStandPhilipIIArena.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="427"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SStandPhilipIIArena.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/To%C5%A1e_Proeski_Arena" title="ToÅ¡e Proeski Arena">ToÅ¡e Proeski Arena</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:HC_Vardar_in_Skopje.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/HC_Vardar_in_Skopje.jpg/220px-HC_Vardar_in_Skopje.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/HC_Vardar_in_Skopje.jpg/330px-HC_Vardar_in_Skopje.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/HC_Vardar_in_Skopje.jpg/440px-HC_Vardar_in_Skopje.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:HC_Vardar_in_Skopje.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The welcoming ceremony for <a href="/wiki/RK_Vardar" title="RK Vardar">RK Vardar</a> after winning the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_EHF_Champions_League" title="2016â17 EHF Champions League">2016â17 EHF Champions League</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">handball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> are the most popular sports in North Macedonia. The <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia_national_football_team" title="North Macedonia national football team">North Macedonia national football team</a> is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_of_Macedonia" title="Football Federation of Macedonia">Football Federation of Macedonia</a>. Their home stadium is the <a href="/wiki/To%C5%A1e_Proeski_Arena" title="ToÅ¡e Proeski Arena">ToÅ¡e Proeski Arena</a>. In November 2003, to celebrate <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>'s jubilee, <a href="/wiki/Darko_Pan%C4%8Dev" title="Darko PanÄev">Darko PanÄev</a> was selected as the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Jubilee_Awards" title="UEFA Jubilee Awards">Golden Player</a> of Macedonia as their most outstanding player of the past 50 years.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[227]</a></sup> He was the winner of the <a href="/wiki/European_Golden_Shoe" title="European Golden Shoe">European Golden Boot</a> award in 1991 and he is best known for scoring the winning penalty in the <a href="/wiki/1991_European_Cup_Final" title="1991 European Cup Final">1991 European Cup Final</a>, bringing <a href="/wiki/Red_Star_Belgrade" title="Red Star Belgrade">Red Star Belgrade</a> the most prestigious trophy in European football for the first time in its 50-year existence. In 2020, the national team qualified for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020" title="UEFA Euro 2020">UEFA Euro 2020</a> (held in 2021), their first major tournament in the country's history.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[228]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Handball is the other important team sport in the country. Macedonian clubs have enjoyed success in European competitions. <a href="/wiki/RK_Vardar" title="RK Vardar">RK Vardar</a> won <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_EHF_Champions_League" title="2016â17 EHF Champions League">2016â17</a> and <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_EHF_Champions_League" title="2018â19 EHF Champions League">2018â19 EHF Champions League</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Kometal_Gjor%C4%8De_Petrov_Skopje" title="Kometal GjorÄe Petrov Skopje">Kometal GjorÄe Petrov Skopje</a> won the 2002 <a href="/wiki/EHF_Champions_League" title="EHF Champions League">EHF Women's Champions League</a>. The <a href="/wiki/European_Women%27s_Handball_Championship" title="European Women's Handball Championship">European Women's Handball Championship</a> took place in 2008 in North Macedonia in Skopje and Ohrid; the <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia_women%27s_national_handball_team" title="North Macedonia women's national handball team">women's national team</a> finished seventh place. The country's <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia_men%27s_national_handball_team" title="North Macedonia men's national handball team">men's national team</a> has appeared in the European and World championships multiple times, with a best finish of fifth at the former (<a href="/wiki/2012_European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship" title="2012 European Men's Handball Championship">2012</a>) and ninth at the latter (<a href="/wiki/2015_World_Men%27s_Handball_Championship" title="2015 World Men's Handball Championship">2015</a>). </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="North Macedonia men's national basketball team">North Macedonia national basketball team</a> represents North Macedonia in international basketball. The team is run by the Basketball Federation of North Macedonia, the governing body of basketball in North Macedonia which was created in 1992 and joined FIBA in 1993. North Macedonia has participated in three <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket" title="EuroBasket">EuroBaskets</a> since then with its best finish at 4th place in <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket_2011" title="EuroBasket 2011">2011</a>. It plays its home games at the <a href="/wiki/Boris_Trajkovski_Sports_Center" title="Boris Trajkovski Sports Center">Boris Trajkovski Sports Center</a> in Skopje. <a href="/wiki/Pero_Anti%C4%87" title="Pero AntiÄ">Pero AntiÄ</a> became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_foreign_NBA_players" title="List of foreign NBA players">first Macedonian basketball player</a> to play in the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a>. He also won three <a href="/wiki/EuroLeague" title="EuroLeague">EuroLeague</a> trophies. </p>
      <p>In the summer months the <a href="/wiki/Ohrid_Swimming_Marathon" title="Ohrid Swimming Marathon">Ohrid Swimming Marathon</a> is an annual event on <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ohrid" title="Lake Ohrid">Lake Ohrid</a> and during the winter months there is skiing in North Macedonia's winter sports centres. North Macedonia also takes part in the Olympic Games. Participation in the Games is organised by the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Committee_of_North_Macedonia" title="Olympic Committee of North Macedonia">Olympic Committee of North Macedonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[229]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Magomed_Ibragimov_(wrestler,_born_1974)" title="Magomed Ibragimov (wrestler, born 1974)">Magomed Ibragimov</a> competed for FYR Macedonia in the <a href="/wiki/Wrestling_at_the_2000_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_freestyle_85_kg" title="Wrestling at the 2000 Summer Olympics â Men's freestyle 85 kg">freestyle 85&nbsp;kg competition</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">2000 Summer Olympics</a> and won the bronze medal, which was the first medal for independent country. Wrestlers <a href="/wiki/Shaban_T%C3%ABrstena" title="Shaban TÃ«rstena">Shaban TÃ«rstena</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shaban_Sejdiu" title="Shaban Sejdiu">Shaban Sejdiu</a> born in North Macedonia, as well as boxers <a href="/wiki/Red%C5%BEep_Red%C5%BEepovski" title="RedÅ¾ep RedÅ¾epovski">RedÅ¾ep RedÅ¾epovski</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ace_Rusevski" title="Ace Rusevski">Ace Rusevski</a>, won Olympic medals as part of Yugoslav Olympic team. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_North_Macedonia" title="Cinema of North Macedonia">Cinema of North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/History_of_film" title="History of film">history of film</a> making in the country dates back over 110&nbsp;years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The first film to be produced on the territory of the present-day the country was made in 1895 by <a href="/wiki/Manakis_brothers" class="mw-redirect" title="Manakis brothers">Janaki and Milton Manaki</a> in Bitola. Throughout the past century, the medium of film has depicted the history, culture and everyday life of the Macedonian people. Over the years many Macedonian films have been presented at film festivals around the world and several of these films have won prestigious awards. The first Macedonian feature film was <i>Frosina</i>, released in 1952 and directed by <a href="/wiki/Vojislav_Nanovi%C4%87" title="Vojislav NanoviÄ">Vojislav NanoviÄ</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[230]</a></sup> The first feature film in colour was <i>Miss Stone</i>, a movie about a Protestant missionary in Ottoman Macedonia. It was released in 1958. The highest grossing feature film in North Macedonia was <i><a href="/wiki/Bal-Can-Can" title="Bal-Can-Can">Bal-Can-Can</a></i>, having been seen by over 500,000 people in its first year alone. In 1994, <a href="/wiki/Milcho_Manchevski" title="Milcho Manchevski">Milcho Manchevski</a>'s film <i><a href="/wiki/Before_the_Rain_(1994_film)" title="Before the Rain (1994 film)">Before the Rain</a></i> was nominated for an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> in the category of <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_International_Feature_Film" title="Academy Award for Best International Feature Film">Best International Feature Film</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[231]</a></sup> Manchevski continues to be the most prominent modern filmmaker in the country having subsequently written and directed <i><a href="/wiki/Dust_(2001_film)" title="Dust (2001 film)">Dust</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Shadows_(2007_film)" title="Shadows (2007 film)">Shadows</a></i>. In 2020, the documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Honeyland_(2019_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Honeyland (2019 film)">Honeyland</a></i> (2019) directed by <a href="/wiki/Tamara_Kotevska" title="Tamara Kotevska">Tamara Kotevska</a> and Ljubomir Stefanov, received nominations in the categories for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_International_Feature_Film" title="Academy Award for Best International Feature Film">Best International Feature Film</a> and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Documentary_Feature" title="Academy Award for Best Documentary Feature">Best Documentary Feature</a> at the <a href="/wiki/92nd_Academy_Awards" title="92nd Academy Awards">92nd Academy Awards</a>, making it the first non-fictional film to receive a nomination in both categories.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[232]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mass_media_in_North_Macedonia" title="Mass media in North Macedonia">Mass media in North Macedonia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The oldest newspaper in the country is <i><a href="/wiki/Nova_Makedonija" title="Nova Makedonija">Nova Makedonija</a></i> from 1944. Other well known newspaper and magazines are: <i><a href="/wiki/Utrinski_vesnik" title="Utrinski vesnik">Utrinski vesnik</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dnevnik_(Skopje)" title="Dnevnik (Skopje)">Dnevnik</a></i>, <i>Vest</i>, <i>Fokus</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Ve%C4%8Der_(Skopje)" class="mw-redirect" title="VeÄer (Skopje)">VeÄer</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Tea_Moderna_(magazine)" title="Tea Moderna (magazine)">Tea Moderna</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Makedonsko_Sonce" title="Makedonsko Sonce">Makedonsko Sonce</a></i>, and <i>Koha</i>. Public channel is <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Radio_Television" title="Macedonian Radio Television">Macedonian Radio Television</a> founded in 1993 by the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_North_Macedonia" title="Assembly of North Macedonia">Assembly of North Macedonia</a>. <a href="/wiki/TEKO_TV" title="TEKO TV">TEKO TV</a> (1989) from <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0tip" title="Å tip">Å tip</a> is the first private television channel in the country. Other popular private channels are: <a href="/wiki/Sitel_(TV_channel)" title="Sitel (TV channel)">Sitel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kanal_5_(Macedonia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kanal 5 (Macedonia)">Kanal 5</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telma_(TV_channel)" title="Telma (TV channel)">Telma</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alfa_TV_(TV_channel_Macedonia)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alfa TV (TV channel Macedonia) (page does not exist)">Alfa TV</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alsat-M" class="mw-redirect" title="Alsat-M">Alsat-M</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-language1-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-language1_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> National and official language in all aspects of the whole territory of the state and in its international relations.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-language2-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-language2_2-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> Co-official language at a state level (excluding defence, central police and monetary policy) and in local self-government units where speakers are 20% or more.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">Ð¡ÐµÐ²ÐµÑÐ½Ð° ÐÐ°ÐºÐµÐ´Ð¾Ð½Ð¸ÑÐ°</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Macedonian" title="Romanization of Macedonian">romanized</a>:&nbsp;</small><i lang="mk-Latn" title="Macedonian-language romanization">Severna Makedonija</i>, <small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Macedonian" title="Help:IPA/Macedonian">[ËsÉvÉrna makÉËdÉnija]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>: <i lang="sq">Maqedonia e Veriut</i>, <small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Albanian" title="Help:IPA/Albanian">[macÉËdÉnja É vÉÉ¾Ëjut]</a></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">Ð ÐµÐ¿ÑÐ±Ð»Ð¸ÐºÐ° Ð¡ÐµÐ²ÐµÑÐ½Ð° ÐÐ°ÐºÐµÐ´Ð¾Ð½Ð¸ÑÐ°</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Macedonian" title="Romanization of Macedonian">romanized</a>:&nbsp;</small><i lang="mk-Latn" title="Macedonian-language romanization">Republika Severna Makedonija</i>, <small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Macedonian" title="Help:IPA/Macedonian">[rÉËpublika ËsÉvÉrna makÉËdÉnija]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>: <i lang="sq">Republika e MaqedonisÃ« sÃ« Veriut</i>, <small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Albanian" title="Help:IPA/Albanian">[rÉËpublika É macÉËdÉnis sÉ vÉÉ¾Ëjut]</a></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-Kosovo-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Kosovo_13-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> Kosovo is the subject of a territorial dispute between the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Republic of Kosovo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Republic of Serbia</a>. The Republic of Kosovo <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">unilaterally declared independence</a> on 17 February 2008. <a href="/wiki/Kosovo%E2%80%93Serbia_relations" title="KosovoâSerbia relations">Serbia continues to claim</a> it as part of its <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">own sovereign territory</a>. The two governments <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Pristina_negotiations" title="BelgradeâPristina negotiations">began to normalise relations</a> in 2013, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">2013 Brussels Agreement</a>. Kosovo is currently recognized as an independent state by <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">98</a> out of the 193 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">United Nations member states</a>. In total, <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">113</a> UN member states recognized Kosovo at some point, of which <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">15</a> later withdrew their recognition. North Macedonia has recognized Kosovo since 9 October 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[239]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">United Nations General Assembly resolution 47/225 of 8 April,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[11]</a></sup> United Nations Security Council <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_817" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 817">Resolutions 817 of 7 April</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_845" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 845">845 of 18 June</a> 1993<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[12]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-111"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-111">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This policy changed after 1943 with the arrival of Tito's envoy Montenegrin Serb <a href="/wiki/Svetozar_Vukmanovi%C4%87" title="Svetozar VukmanoviÄ">Svetozar VukmanoviÄ</a>-Tempo. He began in earnest to organise armed resistance to the Bulgarian rule and sharply criticised <a href="/wiki/Metodi_Shatorov" title="Metodi Shatorov">Sharlo</a>'s pro-Bulgarian policy. At a meeting of the partisan brigades, as well as a group of battalions in the <a href="/wiki/Resen,_North_Macedonia" title="Resen, North Macedonia">Resen</a> region on 21 December 1943, Tempo makes the following comments about Shatorov and the leadership of the MCP: "They thought that the Macedonian people were Bulgarians and that they were oppressed by the hegemony of Great Serbia and had to be transferred to Bulgaria. Their basic slogan is: 'All non-Macedonians out of Macedonia'. The capital <i>J</i> [Serbo-Croatian spelling of Yugoslavia, Yugoslavian, etc.] was deleted from all documents. In fact they did not want Yugoslavia, no matter where it stood politically. When the war started, the initial decision of this leadership was to be separate from Yugoslavia and from Tito. They declared that Macedonia would be free as soon as the Bulgarians came...."</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>

           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-941690-65-2" title="Special:BookSources/0-941690-65-2">0-941690-65-2</a>, p. 114: The "highlanders" or "Makedones" of the mountainous regions of western Macedonia are derived from northwest Greek stock; they were akin both to those who at an earlier time may have migrated south to become the historical "Dorians".</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-25">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Nigel Guy Wilson (2009). <i>Encyclopedia of Ancient Greece</i>, Routledge, p. 439: The latest archaeological findings have confirmed that Macedonia took its name from a tribe of tall, Greek-speaking people, the Makednoi.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFBeekes2010" class="citation cs2"><a href="/wiki/Robert_S._P._Beekes" title="Robert S. P. Beekes">Beekes, Robert</a> (2010), <i>Etymological Dictionary of Greek</i>, <b>II</b>, Leiden, Boston: Brill, p.&nbsp;894</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Etymological+Dictionary+of+Greek&amp;rft.place=Leiden%2C+Boston&amp;rft.pages=894&amp;rft.pub=Brill&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.aulast=Beekes&amp;rft.aufirst=Robert&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANorth+Macedonia" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-27">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFDe_Decker2016" class="citation journal cs1">De Decker, Filip (2016). "AN ETYMOLOGICAL CASE STUDY ON THE AND VOCABULARY IN ROBERT BEEKES'S NEW ETYMOLOGICAL DICTIONARY OF GREEK". <i>Studia Linguistica Universitatis Iagellonicae Cracoviensis</i>. <b>133</b> (2). <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.4467%2F20834624SL.16.006.5152">10.4467/20834624SL.16.006.5152</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Studia+Linguistica+Universitatis+Iagellonicae+Cracoviensis&amp;rft.atitle=AN+ETYMOLOGICAL+CASE+STUDY+ON+THE+AND+VOCABULARY+IN+ROBERT+BEEKES%27S+NEW+ETYMOLOGICAL+DICTIONARY+OF+GREEK&amp;rft.volume=133&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.date=2016&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.4467%2F20834624SL.16.006.5152&amp;rft.aulast=De+Decker&amp;rft.aufirst=Filip&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANorth+Macedonia" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-28">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"What is often overlooked is how Bulgarians and Greeks collaborated unknowingly from the middle decades of the 19th century onward in breathing new life into the geographical name Macedonia, which was all but forgotten during the Byzantine and Ottoman periods. In the late Ottoman period, ââMacedoniaââ as such did not exist as an administrative unit in the empire... Greek nationalism, fixated on the continuity between ancient and modern Hellenes, was keen to project the name Macedonia as a way to assert the Greek historical character of the area. In 1845, for instance, the story of Alexander was published in a Slavo-Macedonian dialect scripted in Greek characters... For their part, Bulgarian nationalists readily accepted Macedonia as a regional denomination... Macedonia had become one of the ââhistoricââ Bulgarian lands... and ââMacedonian Bulgarianââ turned into a standard phrase." Dimitar Bechev, Historical Dictionary of the Republic of Macedonia, Scarecrow Press, 2009, 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0810862956" title="Special:BookSources/0810862956">0810862956</a>, Introduction, p. VII.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-29">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"In the early 19th c. the modern Greeks with their Western-derived obsession with antiquity played a crucial role in reviving the classical name âMacedoniaâ in the popular consciousness of the Balkan peoples. For a thousand years before that the name âMacedoniaâ had meant different things for Westerners and Balkan Christians: for Westerners it always denoted the territories of the ancient Macedonians, but for the Greeks and all other Balkan Christians the name âMacedoniaâ â if at all used â covered the territories of the former Byzantine theme âMacedoniaâ, situated between Adrianople (Edrine) and the river Nestos (Mesta) in classical and present-day Thrace. The central and northern parts of present-day âgeographic Macedoniaâ were traditionally called either âBulgariaâ and âLower Moesiaâ, but within a generation after Greek independence (gained in 1830) these names were replaced by âMacedoniaâ in the minds of both Greeks and non-Greeks." Drezov K. (1999) Macedonian identity: an overview of the major claims. In: Pettifer J. (eds) The New Macedonian Question. St Antony's Series. Palgrave Macmillan, London, 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0230535798" title="Special:BookSources/0230535798">0230535798</a>, pp. 50-51.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"In 1813 Macedonia did not exist. A century later, it had become a hotly contested nationalist cause, a battlefield, and an obsession. What led to this dramatic transformation was modernity: a chilly wind of West European provenance that propelled to the Balkans concepts that few in the region understood, wanted or cared about. Among these, the idea of nationalism was the most potent, and the most lethal. Before the 1850s, Macedonia was a poverty-stricken province of the Ottoman Empire, where an Orthodox Christian and mostly peasant population speaking a variety of Slavonic idioms, Greek, or Vlach, was trying to eke out a modest living, and protect it from rapacious brigands and a decaying Ottoman administrative system. Religion was the only collective identity that most of them could make sense of, for ethnicity and language played little role in shaping their loyalties. But the winds of change quickly gathered momentum, and eventually shattered that multi-ethnic community, producing a 'Greek', or a 'Bulgarian', out of a 'Christian'." D. Livanios' review of Vemund Aarbakke, Ethnic Rivalry and the Quest for Macedonia, 1870-1913 in The Slavonic and East European Review, Vol. 83, No. 1 (Jan., 2005), pp. 141-142</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>The ancient name 'Macedonia' disappeared during the period of Ottoman rule and was only restored in the nineteenth century originally as geographical term.</i> The Oxford Handbook of the History of Nationalism, John Breuilly, Oxford University Press, 2013, 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0199209197" title="Special:BookSources/0199209197">0199209197</a>, p. 192.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-32">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>The region was not called "Macedonia" by the Ottomans, and the name "Macedonia" gained currency together with the ascendance of rival nationalism.</i> Collective Memory, National Identity, and Ethnic Conflict: Greece, Bulgaria, and the Macedonian Question, Victor Roudometof, Greenwood Publishing Group, 2002, 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0275976483" title="Special:BookSources/0275976483">0275976483</a>, p. 89.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>The Greeks were amongst the first to define these lands since the beginning of the 19th century. For educated Greeks, Macedonia was the historical Greek land of kings Philip and Alexander the Great.</i> John S. Koliopoulos, Thanos M. Veremis, Modern Greece: A History since 1821. A New History of Modern Europe, John Wiley &amp; Sons, 2009, 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1444314831" title="Special:BookSources/1444314831">1444314831</a>, p. 48.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Donald Bloxham, The Final Solution: A Genocide, OUP Oxford, 2009, 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0199550336" title="Special:BookSources/0199550336">0199550336</a>, p. 65.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Chris Kostov, Contested Ethnic Identity: The Case of Macedonian Immigrants in Toronto, Peter Lang, 2010,

           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFRothBrunnbauer2008" class="citation book cs1">Roth, Klaus; Brunnbauer, Ulf (2008). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=6RveDmHbIv8C&amp;pg=PA136"><i>Region, Regional Identity and Regionalism in Southeastern Europe</i></a>.          <li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-75">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFShaw1977" class="citation book cs1">Shaw, Stanford J. (1977). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=AIET_7ji7YAC&amp;pg=PA209"><i>History of the Ottoman Empire and Modern Turkey: Volume 2, Reform, Revolution, and Republic: The Rise of Modern Turkey 1808â1975</i></a>. Cambridge University Press. p.&nbsp;209. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-521-29166-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-521-29166-8"><bdi>978-0-521-29166-8</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=History+of+the+Ottoman+Empire+and+Modern+Turkey%3A+Volume+2%2C+Reform%2C+Revolution%2C+and+Republic%3A+The+Rise+of+Modern+Turkey+1808%E2%80%931975&amp;rft.pages=209&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=1977&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-521-29166-8&amp;rft.aulast=Shaw&amp;rft.aufirst=Stanford+J.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DAIET_7ji7YAC%26pg%3DPA209&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANorth+Macedonia" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-76"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-76">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There was even an attempt to form a kind of revolutionary government led by the socialist Nikola Karev. The Krushevo manifesto was declared, assuring the population that the uprising was against the Sultan and not against Muslims in general, and that all peoples would be included. As the population of Krushevo was two-thirds hellenised Vlachs and Patriarchist Slavs, this was a wise move. Despite these promises, the insurgent flew Bulgarian flags everywhere and in many places the uprising did entail attacks on Muslim Turks and Albanians who themselves organised for self-defence." Who are the Macedonians? Hugh Poulton, C. Hurst &amp; Co. Publishers, 1995, 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1850652384" title="Special:BookSources/1850652384">1850652384</a>, p. 57.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-77"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-77">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In fact Macedonian historians as <a href="/wiki/Blaze_Ristovski" class="mw-redirect" title="Blaze Ristovski">Blaze Ristovski</a> have recognized, that the "government" of the "republic", nowadays a symbol of Macedonian statehood, was actually composed of people who identified themselves as "Greeks", "Vlachs" and "Bulgarians". "We, the People: Politics of National Peculiarity in Southeastern Europe" Diana Mishkova, Central European University Press, 2009, 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9639776289" title="Special:BookSources/9639776289">9639776289</a>, p. 124.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-78">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"The IMARO activists saw the future autonomous Macedonia as a multinational polity, and did not pursue the self-determination of Macedonian Slavs as a separate ethnicity. Therefore, Macedonian was an umbrella term covering Bulgarians, Turks, Greeks, Vlachs, Albanians, Serbs, Jews, and so on." Historical Dictionary of Macedonia, Historical Dictionaries of Europe, Dimitar Bechev, Scarecrow Press, 2009, 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0810862956" title="Special:BookSources/0810862956">0810862956</a>, Introduction.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-79">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The political and military leaders of the Slavs of Macedonia at the turn of the century seem not to have heard the call for a separate Macedonian national identity; they continued to identify themselves in a national sense as Bulgarians rather than Macedonians.[...] (They) never seem to have doubted "the predominantly Bulgarian character of the population of Macedonia". "The Macedonian conflict: ethnic nationalism in a transnational world", Princeton University Press, Danforth, Loring M. 1997, 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0691043566" title="Special:BookSources/0691043566">0691043566</a>, p. 64.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-80"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-80">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">TasiÄ, Dmitar, The Macedonian Youth Secret Revolutionary Organization (MYSRO) 1922-1927: A New Moment in Macedonian Struggle. Storia e Regione. 2019, Vol. 28, Issue 1, pp. 22-43.</span> </li>

         <li id="cite_note-109"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-109">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Bulgaria managed to save its entire 48,000-strong Jewish population during World War II from deportation to <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">Nazi concentration camps</a>, but under German pressure those Jews from their newly annexed territories without Bulgarian citizenship were deported, such as those from Vardar Macedonia and <a href="/wiki/Western_Thrace" title="Western Thrace">Western Thrace</a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ushmm.org/wlc/article.php?lang=en&amp;ModuleId=10006804"><i>The Holocaust in Macedonia: Deportation of Monastir Jewry</i></a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Holocaust_Memorial_Museum" title="United States Holocaust Memorial Museum">United States Holocaust Memorial Museum</a></span> </li>

                   <ul>
                    <li><sup>1</sup> <a href="/wiki/Island#Oceanic_islands" title="Island">Oceanic islands</a> within the vicinity of Europe are usually grouped with the continent even though they are not situated on its continental shelf.</li>
